A Historical Account of the Xinjiang Incident (Part 1) 82

— Kashgar Correspondence.

The situation of the recent incident in Xinjiang has been reported in newspapers from time to time, but unfortunately, the information is limited and unsystematic, which may not attract the attention of readers. I have just arrived in Kashgar (i.e., Shufu) and happened to witness this disaster. Now, I will provide a brief report of what I have heard and seen, as well as the various sufferings I have personally experienced, to readers far away in the interior.

The causes of this rebellion in Xinjiang are complex. Initially, Jin Shuren's misgovernment (the details of which cannot be described in detail due to time constraints) led to a popular anti-government trend. However, there was no tendency towards any violent uprising because although the ethnic groups in Xinjiang have always harbored hatred towards the Han people, they lack the ability to act independently (their character is mostly foolish). Without outside forces taking the initiative, they would have no possibility of acting independently. Now, the ambitious bandit leader from Gansu, Ma Zhongying, whose ambitions have not died (he originally intended to seize Xinjiang to establish his special Muslim power, which is well known and cannot be concealed), intends to stage a comeback. He learned from his failure to incite rebellion in Hami last year, so in addition to notifying the encircling Hui people who were resisting in that area in advance, he also colluded with Provincial Army and Chen Ma Fuming (a Muslim from Hezhou) as internal allies. (The regiment happened to be stationed in the Shanshan and Turpan area.) Also, because he had just been recruited by the central government, it was inconvenient for him to openly enter Xinjiang with a large force. Therefore, he only sent a plainclothes team of 37 people to Xinjiang first to engage in agitation and incitement. Once the chaos spread and the Provincial Army was unable to defend against it, they could use the excuse of popular opinion to ask him to come out of the mountains to quell the rebellion. He could then seize Xinjiang without making a sound, while still maintaining the pretense of not breaking away from the central government, controlling the ambitions of Britain and Russia. The cunning of his plan is evident here. Who knew that his ignorant plainclothes team would gradually reveal their intentions to others, intentionally or unintentionally, when they saw that everything was going smoothly? However, after the 37 people left the mountains, they knew that there was a large force blocking their path in Hami, making it difficult to pass through. Therefore, they took a detour through the mountains to Shanshan (the city is near the mountains) and reached their destination. Due to Ma Fuming's internal support, Shanshan and Turpan soon fell one after another. The bandits now occupied two cities, had a regiment of soldiers, and a large number of supporting Hui people. Their momentum grew daily. At this time, the Provincial Army was far away in Hami and was being held back by the bandits who were resisting. They had to transfer troops nearby to suppress the rebellion, but ultimately failed to recover the cities due to the large number of Hui people. The bandits then divided their forces into two routes, one attacking the provincial capital and the other taking the Southern Route (i.e., the South Xinjiang Road). The bandits who took the Southern Route relied on the power of the local Hui people to attack, causing the counties along the route to fall one after another. They then advanced to Yanqi and established a general headquarters there, calling themselves the Yanqi Bandit Suppression Command of the 36th Division. At this time, the transportation between Kashgar and Dihua was cut off. All subsequent documents and telegrams had to be routed through Yili, around the Bing Daban Pass, and to Aksu before being relayed to Kashgar. Every message took more than twenty days. The local Hui people in various places in southern Xinjiang were also ready to move, many secretly preparing weapons. For example, the case of investigating iron bars in Moyu County and the case of confiscating large-headed clubs in Yingjisha County (made of strong wood, over three feet long, thick at one end, and filled with iron nails at the thick end). Although the authorities discovered this, they dared not pursue the matter for fear of provoking a popular uprising. The Hui people saw through this weakness and became even more unscrupulous. Later, almost every person had a large-headed club or iron bar and roamed the countryside. At this time, we Han people feared being attacked by them and did not dare to travel even a step away. Even if we had to go to the countryside for business, we had to go in groups and carry weapons, but we were still very cautious and did not dare to stay for long. The authorities' fear of provoking a popular uprising and their tolerance of everything was a cautious approach, but this kind of popular uprising had already shown signs of erupting, even without provocation. Unfortunately, the authorities were unaware and indulged in complacency, leading to the current chaotic situation. What else can be said? At this time, Ma Shiming, who was entrenched in Yanqi, took advantage of this opportunity to send his followers to the areas of Luntai, Kuqa, and Baicheng to actively incite and spread propaganda (claiming to be acting on the central government's orders to overthrow Jin and save the people). The general ignorant Hui people echoed his calls. Kuqa was originally a place that had been rebellious for a long time (it had rebelled twice in 1918 and 1923). The Hui people of the county, Temier (who was a porter head in Kuqa County, known as a "carriage household township chief" in Xinjiang), gathered Hui people and secretly organized. As a result, Luntai, Kuqa, Toksu, Shaya, Korla, Baicheng, and other counties rebelled one after another. All Han women were raped and occupied, and all Han people who resided there, whether travelers or permanent residents, were brutally killed. Luntai was particularly tragic compared to other places. It is said that most of the Han people who died were beaten to death with clubs, because at that time, the weapons they used, apart from the few firearms seized from the government army, were mostly large-headed wooden clubs. In addition, all Han people's property, whether the owner was present or not, was looted. At this time, the rebels' slogan was to build Islam (meaning Islam), advocating killing Han people and reviving the Hui people. As a result, the Hui people in southern Xinjiang were incited. At this time, the rebels were approaching Aksu. Jin Shuzhi, the commander of the Kashgar Garrison (Jin Shuren's fourth younger brother, who had no political or military knowledge, was extravagant, and specialized in extorting money), was panicked when he heard the news and immediately sent Regiment Commander Yang Qingming with two companies of cavalry to defend. (They departed on January 30th.) Commander Jin was still afraid that his forces were insufficient and discussed with Tao Yin Ma Shaowu (a Yunnan Hui Muslim) several times to appoint Li Denglong, the adjutant-general of the division, as the commander of the second route to assist Aksu. Just as they were preparing to depart, they received news of a rebellion by the Hui people in Leyu County (in southern Xinjiang, forty miles from Hetian). All Han people, from the county magistrate downwards, were beaten to death with large-headed clubs. Hotan, Lop, and Keriya counties also rose up in succession. Pishan, Yecheng, Zepu, Yarkand, and Shache counties also sent urgent reports one after another. Commander Jin saw that the general situation was over and was heartbroken. The next night, he announced that he had suddenly died of an illness. After Jin Shuzhi's death, military power was transferred to Ma Shaowu. At this time, Aksu had already fallen. Regiment Commander Yang retreated to Bachu. Kashgar's Hui and Han cities (Shufu, where the Tao Yin was located, and Shule, where the commander was located) were in extreme danger. Tao Yin Ma was originally the leader of the New Sect of Islam, and he thought that he could pacify the people's hearts through his religious connections. Therefore, he sent people to Hotan and the surrounding areas to offer comfort and ordered the second route to assist the Aksu army to depart. When they arrived at Jiutai (a station name, two stations below Bachu), they encountered the rebels. The two armies were in a stalemate for nearly two months. During that time, the Kashgar army won several battles, killing nearly a thousand enemies, but due to the disparity in numbers and the disorganization of the army, they ultimately failed. Commander Li died in battle. At this time, Commander Ma received a telegram from the Provincial Government appointing him as the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in Southern Xinjiang. He then appointed Si Xingyang (from Gansu), Li's staff officer, as the commander. He was inexperienced and young and was not from the military. As a result, the army was dissatisfied, and internal conflicts arose from time to time. Ma continued to send Liu Ding (from Gansu), the chief of staff and regiment commander of the division, as the commander of the third route to assist Aksu. However, Liu had previously instigated discord between Commander Jin Shuzhi and Ma Shaowu, and he was mediocre and timid. On the front line, he had disagreements with Commander Si, leading to constant disputes. As a result, the military situation on the front line became increasingly chaotic. At this time, Commander Ma saw the situation on the front line and knew that it was difficult to win. In addition, the consolations in Hotan and other places were ineffective, so he changed his plan to make peace and sent representatives to welcome the rebels to Kashgar. Both sides then stopped military action. Ma took advantage of this ceasefire to send a telegram to the front, ordering Liu to secretly send a team to Hetian to quell the rebellion. However, Liu refused, saying that the rebels had not retreated. Ma could do nothing. At that time, several of Ma's trusted officers offered advice to Ma, urging him to recruit Burut people (a nomadic people who live deep in the mountains, also known as Black Tartars, referred to as Bu people for short) for assistance to alleviate the temporary emergency. However, some people said that these people were originally ruthless bandits who did not know human nature and could not be relied upon to help the Han people defend the territory. After considering it, Ma Shaowu finally adopted this strategy. In less than half a month, he recruited seven or eight hundred people, formed them into a regiment, and gave them four hundred rifles and two cannons. At the same time, he recruited two battalions of Hui soldiers and one company of special forces (a mixture of Han and Hui), and after the organization was completed, he appointed Company Commander Chen (a Shandong Hui Muslim) as the regiment commander to lead a regiment of Bu soldiers to Suhongka (a small road leading to Dashi) to prevent the rebels from attacking Kashgar by detouring through the Dashi small road. He also sent two additional battalions of the new army to Pishan to block the path of the bandits from Hotan, Changyu, and other places to Kashgar. The cause of the Hotan uprising was that Yan, the magistrate of Leyu County, was greedy and insatiable. Also, because he served two terms (since Jin Shuren took office in Xinjiang, it was stipulated that the term of office for each county magistrate would be limited to one year. Yan and Jin were both from Gansu, so Yan was given two terms). Moreover, the staff used in the office were generally local ruffians, who colluded with each other, leading to a popular uprising. Therefore, the rebel leader Yimir (from Moyu County, about thirty years old, was a Hui scholar, now called "Pasha Pasha," which means Hui King) gathered a crowd to riot and attacked the county office, killing Yan's entire family. He then broke through Hotan. It is said that not many Han people were killed in Hetian, but their property was confiscated, and they were reduced to beggars.

Director Yu's Speech at the Baojia Conference of Counties South of the Yangtze River 83

— Continued

The Baojia compilation and investigation procedure consists of three phases. Currently, ten counties have completed the third phase of work: Tongshan, Fengxian, Xiaoxian, Jingjiang, Qidong, Yancheng, Gaoyou, Gaoyou, Xinghua, Dongtai, and Shiying. Five counties are about to complete the third phase of work: Rugao, Nantong, Suqian, and Chongming. Six counties are currently in the third phase of work: Peixian, Ganxian, Pixian, Suining, and Haimen, Huaiyin. Three counties have just begun the third phase of work: Siyang, Changshan, and Huaian. Three counties are currently in the second phase of work: Donghai, Guanyun, and Muyang. As for the content of the work in each county, some counties have progressed quickly and the work is practical and correct, some counties have progressed slowly but the work is correct and practical, some counties have progressed quickly but the work is incorrect and impractical, and a few counties have even made mistakes of perfunctory and hypocrisy. What we hope for first is correctness and practicality, and second is speed. We believe that it is acceptable and productive to delay the time slightly for the sake of correctness and practicality. For example, Peixian is a good example. The most unacceptable thing is to be perfunctory and sloppy. Even if the three phases of such work are completed, we will definitely punish them to redo it. These counties with achievements will be announced after all the work is completed in the future. In short, in the Baojia work of the counties north of the Yangtze River this time, several counties in the Tongshan area have done very well, and several counties in the Donghai area have also done well. Jingjiang in the Nantong area has also done well. The counties that have done well have now shown great results. The Xuhai area has always been a region with many bandits. Every time the crops are growing, bandits rise up like hair. This summer, the counties were able to pass through peacefully, and several counties cannot but attribute it to Baojia. The most obvious fact is that, first, bad people have no one to guarantee them and cannot stand in society; second, in kidnapping cases, the hostages cannot find a hiding place. There are also several counties that can actively use Baojia to carry out the work of prohibiting smoking and foot binding, such as Xiaoxian and Suining. In Xiaoxian, it has also achieved great results. The people of Xiaoxian are grateful for the benefits of Baojia. Many two surnames who have long had deep feuds and have not interacted in the countryside are now happy to guarantee each other. The people of Xiaoxian are now even automatically asking the county magistrate to extend the time for training the Baojia chiefs. Generally speaking, the Baojia work of the counties this time is flawed but practical and hardworking, so the results of the compilation and investigation in each county are generally correct. As for the general shortcomings, the first is the lack of preparatory work before the event. The first lack is the work of publicity. The illiterate people are naturally ignorant. If they do not pay attention to the meaning of the Baojia system, they will not understand its usefulness. Therefore, it causes many people's doubts, misunderstandings, and even disputes, which delays the progress of the work. If there is widespread publicity and forceful publicity in advance, these troubles will naturally be reduced or even not occur. The second lack is the work of training. The members of the compilation and investigation committee, the district chiefs, and even the personnel in the county government who are handling the Baojia work are all personnel who are actually engaged in the Baojia work. They should have sufficient training in advance. They should thoroughly understand all the laws and regulations of Baojia. They should be prepared to answer all the practical problems and difficulties. However, most of the counties did not do this work sufficiently, so these workers often make mistakes in their actual work, which affects the efficiency of the work. The third is the lack of communication. The Baojia is to organize the people of the whole county, which is closely related to the interests of all the good people in the county. We should invite all the powerful groups and powerful elements in the county to participate and work together, such as the Party Headquarters, schools, mass organizations, and all other legitimate organizations. We should contact them and invite them. In this way, the work can proceed smoothly. There are many counties that understand this principle and do so, but most counties have not paid attention to this and are only working hard on their own. No wonder everyone is doing weak and hoarse work.

Everyone, now holding Baojia has gotten a lot of cheapness, and the experience of counties north of the Yangtze River in doing Baojia has become our teaching and our borrowing. I would now like to bring up a few things from the actual experience aspect for your attention: First, pay attention to the preparatory work before the event. The so-called preparatory work is the publicity work, training work, and communication work just mentioned, as well as other material preparations, that is, the preparation of all utensils. Everything is established if prepared in advance. Do not dig a well when you are thirsty. Do not be busy and sloppy. Second, carefully select the members of the compilation and investigation committee. If the members of the compilation and investigation committee are not selected well, the work of compilation and investigation cannot be done well. Those who have no sense of responsibility are not allowed. Those who cannot endure hardship are not allowed. Those who specialize in mixing up the errand are not allowed. Third, follow the working procedures set by the department. The department sets three phases of work, and each phase has a special nature. There is a certain procedure in fact. If you are curious and do not follow this procedure, or if you try to be clever and advance together, you will inevitably mess up the steps and inevitably get incorrect results. Reorganizing it will inevitably waste a lot of time and money. This is already a lesson of fact. Fourth, carefully select the Baojia chief. The purpose of Baojia is to unite good people and eliminate bad people. If you are not careful in selecting the Baojia chief and choose bad people instead, it is better not to do Baojia. If it is found in the future that bad people have become Baojia chiefs, we must quickly move one of your places with command and do a compilation and investigation test area. In this area, all the compilation and investigation personnel will be gathered to do a thorough test and practice, and then gradually give it to other areas. This method has been effective, and you are worth emulating. Sixth, actually get the joint guarantee and the core of the joint result. It must be handled in accordance with the prescribed procedures. Do not be perfunctory and careless.

Finally, I hope that you will first be practical in your work and never have a perfunctory heart. We want to sweep away all the perfunctory and hypocritical faults of the past counties in handling population, investigation, and handling letters, etc. Otherwise, we will end up with the result of wasting money and hurting people, and we will be the sinners of Baojia. Second, we must be quick in our work. Perfunctory is certainly not allowed, and delay is not allowed. We must take the lead, do it in one go, and quickly organize the Baojia in each county to complete our purpose of self-government and self-defense as soon as possible. However, it is certainly not allowed to intentionally delay and hinder the progress of the work, but it is also not allowed to intentionally be clever and hinder the practicality of the work. Third, I hope that you will always go to the countryside and, in accordance with the provisions of the schedule, visit each district in person during the first phase and convene the people to talk about the significance of holding Baojia. During the second phase, visit each district in person and give lectures to the Baojia chiefs of each district and township on the significance and methods of compilation and investigation. During the third phase, visit each district in person and conduct spot checks on households in accordance with the table.

The members of the compilation and investigation committee in each district have also been selected and appointed by the county government: Gao Baozhen in the first district, Qin Jiarui in the second district, Wu Fuzeng in the third district, Zhu Nai'ao in the fourth district, and Sheng Xiangjun in the fifth district.

Songjiang 85

Gu Surname in Tinglin Wutu Robbed

The home of Gu Jinxiang, a farmer in Dayang Wutu, Tinglin, Punan, was broken into by five robbers with a guest accent at about 12 o'clock on the night of the 26th. Each robber held a rifle, and iron bell, etc. and broke in from the side door of the house. One robber tied Gu's feet and threatened him with the muzzle of a gun against his chest. The remaining robbers searched the room, robbing one gong, two pieces of cloth, three silver earrings, and forty-five yuan in cash. After the robbery, they fled back the same way. The victim had foot injuries. A wooden-handled iron bell and a pistol bullet left by the robbers have not yet been reported. After the Director of the First Branch Bureau Li Zeshi found out, he went to inspect the scene and reported it to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Public Security Bureau Appoints Inspectors 86

The County Public Security Bureau recently appointed Yang Shijie as an inspector and Yao Xigui as an inspector. The appointment orders were issued yesterday and distributed to each of them to take office. According to Yang Shijie, he previously served as an inspector and the captain of the Detective Team during the tenure of the former Director Shen, and he solved major cases one after another. Especially when the Pudong bandit Taibao Ashu was wreaking havoc in the counties of Songjiang, Jinshan, and Fengxian, he accompanied the army to search for the remaining bandits and made great efforts to clear the area as soon as possible. Now that Director He has appointed him as an inspector, he will surely be able to help in the future arrests.

Suzhou 87

Creditors of the Xingye Bank File a Lawsuit

The Suzhou branch of the Shanghai China Yuye Bank closed down last month due to the influence of the Shanghai head office. The branch was managed by Wu Songlu and Qin Xinmin. Since the bank's closure, they have been avoiding meeting with anyone. The creditors have organized a creditors' group at the Central Hotel to pursue compensation. Because the managers ignored the creditors' group, a representative meeting was held the day before yesterday (the 29th) in the evening to discuss methods of pursuing debt recovery. It was resolved that all creditors would jointly file a lawsuit with the Wuxian District Court against Wu Songlu and Qin Xinmin, demanding that they be ordered to compensate the full amount.

Various Industries Oppose the National Goods Exhibition 88

The major stores on Guanjian Street in Suzhou City, etc., have strongly opposed the national goods mobile exhibition organized by Sun Zicheng and others, claiming it promotes national goods but is actually for personal gain. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that on the afternoon of the 29th, representatives from the silk industry, foreign and domestic goods industry, foreign and domestic cloth industry, thread industry, and hat industry associations, including Tu Haoquan and Wu Jiyuan, took a petition with signatures from over a hundred stores to the county chamber of commerce. The purpose of the petition was to request that since the chamber advocates for national goods, it should change the mobile exhibition to an exhibition hall and not engage in retail or wholesale sales to protect the business of stores in various industries during the winter season. The chamber of commerce was holding a temporary meeting that day and immediately brought the matter up for discussion, deciding to send a letter to the national goods mobile exhibition, requesting that it be changed to an exhibition hall. It is also reported that the stores have been sending letters to national goods manufacturers in Shanghai, asking them not to participate to avoid damaging relations.

Changshu 89

Dispute Over the Education Bureau's Distribution of Funds

The principals of the county's elementary schools recently discovered that the Education Bureau Director, Lu Jingmo, had reported to the education authorities that the expenses for the seventh, eighth, and ninth months of this year had been fully disbursed. However, each school only received 50% of the funds for August and September. Feeling confused and alarmed, they jointly inquired with the bureau. Director Lu stated that the schools had no right to inquire, and they did not receive a satisfactory explanation. The principals then petitioned the county government. The county magistrate, in addition to reviewing the bureau's submitted documents, promised the schools a detailed investigation. This occurred on the 25th of this month. Now, on the 29th, the bureau disbursed 50% of the September funds. The principals seized this opportunity to express their dissatisfaction and again asked the director for clarification. At the same time, the County Education Association, believing that Director Lu's report to superiors was inaccurate and that a significant amount of funds was missing (approximately 10,000 yuan), sent representatives to the bureau to audit the accounts. Upon hearing this news, the director, fearing a scandal, went into hiding and could not be found. According to bureau personnel, he claimed to have requested leave to go to the provincial capital, but no leave request had been received during the day.

Wuxi 90

Oil Mills Oppose Grain Tax in Anhui Province

The Anhui Provincial Government recently stipulated that a grain tax of five liters per stone would be levied on grain leaving the province, including soybeans. The oil mills in this county rely on soybeans imported from Anhui as their raw material. This year, Anhui suffered from severe drought, drastically reducing soybean production. Moreover, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces also experienced drought, leading to sluggish sales of soybean cakes and making it difficult for the mills to sustain themselves. Now, Anhui Province suddenly imposed a grain tax of 5%, directly increasing the burden on the oil mill industry and indirectly harming rural areas. Therefore, they specially sent a letter to the county chamber of commerce yesterday, requesting that they telegraph the National Government, the Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry, urging them to order the Anhui Provincial Government to amend its regulations and exclude soybeans to alleviate business difficulties and benefit farmers. Furthermore, the tobacco, hardware, and electrical materials industries in this county stated that business has been declining in recent years, with sales less than half of what they used to be, yet the business tax rate has not been reduced. Therefore, they specially proposed at a meeting of the county chamber of commerce members that a telegram be sent to the ministries and provinces yesterday, requesting a general 50% reduction in the business tax rate to alleviate their hardships.

Provincial Order to Postpone Land Value Tax Collection 91

The land value declaration for the city of Wuxi, which was originally scheduled to be completed in two months after the door-to-door declaration began, from September 1st to the end of October, has been delayed due to continuous telegrams to the central and provincial governments from local public organizations and urban residents, expressing their difficulties and requesting postponement, as well as petitions to Beijing and the provincial capital. Yan Shenyu, the county magistrate of Wuxi, recognizing that Wuxi has suffered from consecutive years of disasters, business decline, and rural bankruptcy, coupled with this year's drought, which has severely impacted the urban economy, believed that if the land tax were levied immediately after the land value declaration, the people would be unable to bear it. However, the land value declaration is an important task for implementing the Prime Minister's legacy and reorganizing land values, and it should be completed on schedule. He immediately submitted a report to the provincial government, requesting instructions. Yesterday, he received an order from the provincial government stating: "The purpose of the provincial government's organization of the city land value declaration in your county is to reorganize land administration, which is a very important task. You must complete it on schedule and not delay it in any way. As for the request to temporarily postpone the collection of land value tax, it should be approved." Magistrate Yan, upon receiving the order, immediately issued a notice to all businesses in the city, granting a one-month extension until the end of November. They must complete the declaration form within the deadline and not hesitate any longer. Yesterday afternoon, he also summoned the township heads of the city's thirty-five townships to the county government to talk, instructing them to provide practical assistance to facilitate progress.

Changzhou 92

Chamber of Commerce Requests Abolition of Tax Collection by Brokerage Firms

Representatives from various industries gathered to discuss the issue of brokerage firms collecting business tax. The results were as follows: The Ministry of Finance believes that the practice of brokerage firms collecting business tax from merchants conflicts with the business tax law, and the National Finance Conference has resolved to reform the practice of brokerage firms collecting taxes as soon as possible. The brokerage firms in this county unanimously agree with the Wuxi Chamber of Commerce and propose: 1. Send a letter to the Wuxi Chamber of Commerce and convene brokerage firms from neighboring counties to collect opinions and proceed together. 2. Send a telegram to the central government requesting the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance to abolish the practice in accordance with the ministry's order, and send a letter to the business tax bureau for its information.

Hangzhou 93

Borrowing 900,000 for Road Construction

The road construction funds in Zhejiang Province are still short by over 3 million yuan. The Construction Department previously sent representatives to Wuhan to borrow 1.2 million yuan from the Four Provinces Farmers Bank, which, together with previous loans, amounted to 3 million yuan. A portion of the road assets in eastern Zhejiang and 1 million yuan in local public bonds were used as collateral. Recently, Xu Ziqing, the manager of the bank, came to Hangzhou, and Zeng Yangfu, the director of the Construction Department, met with him to discuss the matter. The outcome was satisfactory, and it is reported that the loan has been reduced to 900,000 yuan, with the same collateral as before. Other conditions are still being discussed, and it is hoped that an agreement can be reached next month.

Zhenjiang 94

Silver Shop Carelessly Loses Tens of Thousands

Wenhua Silver Shop, located at the entrance of Tianzhu Street in this port, has been in business for over thirty years. It has a strong capital base and has made considerable profits in the past. However, in recent years, due to the decline of the market and rural bankruptcy, its business has declined sharply, barely managing to survive. Unfortunately, yesterday (the 29th) at around 10 a.m., while the shop was conducting business, a fire suddenly broke out on the upper floor in the middle. The staff knew it was difficult to extinguish and hurriedly took out several account books and the gold jewelry in the cabinets, fleeing outside. In an instant, the fire spread rapidly. The fire brigade arrived after hearing the news and tried their best to put out the fire. It was finally extinguished by noon. The shop, with three courtyards, was completely destroyed, leaving only the storefront. The total loss is estimated at around 30,000 yuan. It is reported that they only have over 10,000 yuan in fire insurance. The neighboring Gongji Pharmacy, although not burned, suffered several thousand yuan in damage due to water damage.

Shaoxing 95

Ma'an Township Residents Repair Sandbar Dikes

The sandbars outside the dikes in Ma'an Township, Shaoxing, have been repeatedly eroded by storm surges in recent years, with over 2,000 mu collapsing. Recently, in the afternoon, the outer sea tides overflowed, causing widespread flooding, which destroyed crops, livestock, and residents' houses, resulting in heavy losses for the sandbar residents. Currently, residents in the area, including Xu, have initiated the construction of a large dike, over ten li long, from Meiyao Ditch to Tongjia Pagoda, to prevent tidal water from entering. Due to the large expenses, they jointly requested subsidies from the county yesterday.

The Yinxian County Games, which opened on the 25th, concluded yesterday (the 28th) on the fourth day. After the field events concluded in the morning, a 10,000-meter race was temporarily held for the public group. Jin Limin of the Ningbo Public Security Bureau Police Brigade won first place with a time of 37 minutes and 63 seconds, breaking the previous record. After four days of competition, the award ceremony was held that afternoon. The Shiqi Elementary School won the overall championship with three first-place finishes.

The Shanghai Customs Issued a Notice on the Collection of the Balanced Tax Law 102

No Refund of Unsurcharged Additional Tax

Tang Haian, the superintendent of the Shanghai Customs, and Berle, the director of the Tax Bureau, issued Notice No. 1394 yesterday to promulgate the method of collecting the silver export balance tax as required by the present regulations. It reads: "It has been ordered that the tax rate for silver export tax be formulated and posted in Notice No. 1389. Now, according to the government's order, the method of collecting the silver export balance tax is stipulated as follows: 1. This balance tax does not include the disaster relief surtax and the customs surtax. 2. The tax rate for this balance tax shall be based on the date of reporting silver export, and not on the date of shipment of the export ship. 3. Once this balance tax has been collected, if the silver reported for export is stopped from shipment, it will not be refunded. Let all merchants be aware of this and hereby announce it."

New Stamp Tax Tickets Were Issued in Advance Yesterday 103

Implementation of the New Stamp Tax Law Is Pending

The Ministry of Finance announced the new Stamp Tax Law, which will be implemented tomorrow, and reissued the Shih Ta pattern. New stamp tax tickets will also be sold by post offices on the same day. However, in Shanghai, for the convenience of merchants, sales began yesterday. However, the new Stamp Tax Law will not be implemented until it is promulgated by the National Government. The news is summarized as follows:

Post Office Notice 104

The Postal Administration posted Notice No. 1176 yesterday, which reads: "It has been decided that new stamp tax tickets will be sold in post offices across the country from November 1st, as previously announced in Notice No. 1171. Now, in order to meet the needs of the public, the stamp tax tickets will be sold in advance from October 30th at all post offices in Shanghai. This is to inform everyone." Therefore, there was a crowd of buyers yesterday.

Tax Agency Letter 105

The Tax Agency of the Ministry of Finance sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, which reads: "Dear Sirs, upon reading your newspaper of October 30th, the news that the new stamp tax would be issued today, the statement that the Ministry of Finance announced the new Stamp Tax Law to be implemented on the first day of next month is not in accordance with the facts. Although this new Stamp Tax Law has been passed by the Legislative Yuan, it has not yet been promulgated and implemented by the National Government. Before it is promulgated and implemented, the current Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax will still apply. We are afraid that merchants may misunderstand, so we send this letter to you and hope you will check and correct it. Sincerely, the Tax Agency of the Ministry of Finance, October 30th."

Haiyuan Can Arrive Today 106

Overseas Chinese Unemployed in the Netherlands

Visiting Ships to Carry Them Back Home

The first ship, Haiyuan, newly built by the China Merchants Bureau in England, did not stay long when it arrived in Hong Kong and immediately started work in Shanghai. It was reported that it had passed Xiamen the day before yesterday at noon. Yesterday at noon, a telegram came saying that it had passed Wenzhou Yang and was expected to arrive in Shanghai this afternoon. The Bureau received a telegram and hired a pilot to guide it to the Tongsha Ocean. It is expected to arrive at the Jin Liyuan Wharf at 3 p.m. The ship will fly the British flag on its way to China. Only after the ship is handed over in Shanghai will the flag be changed.

Carrying overseas Chinese home According to a letter from the British Embassy, there are more than 500 overseas Chinese unemployed in the Netherlands. Whether the Haiyuan will load them all or send them back in batches was not stated in detail in the telegram. Therefore, the number of people is unknown and will be known after the ship arrives.

Factory inspection The Haiyuan was built by the Swan Hunter shipyard in England. According to the contract, the ship will be handed over in Shanghai. The shipyard is responsible for everything on the way. Therefore, the chimney has not yet been painted yellow. After arriving in port this afternoon, it must enter the Jiangnan Factory to inspect the ship's body. If there is nothing wrong, it can be officially accepted. The ship is 343 feet long, 47 feet wide, and 25 feet high to the upper deck and 17 feet and 6 inches high to the clear deck. It can carry 3,200 tons of cargo and travels at 13 knots per hour. The ship has an automatic water meter, direction finder, anti-theft device, and electricity.

Foreign ships depreciate The Haiyuan was originally scheduled to run the Shanghai-Shantou-Hong Kong-Guangdong route and also run Qingdao. However, due to the extended route and the need to stop, each shift takes seven days more, which is not cost-effective. Therefore, Hua Hongsheng decided not to run Qingdao and only run the Shanghai-Shantou-Hong Kong-Guangdong route. Foreign merchants such as Taikoo Company heard that the new ship had arrived in Shanghai. Once the shift started, it would have an impact on the shipping industry. Therefore, the South China water fee had already been reduced by 20% to compete.

International Trade Bureau 109

Introduce Mineral Products

The United Kingdom Needs Graphite, Tungsten, Antimony, Lead and Tin

Mineral Exporters Can Contact the Bureau

The United Kingdom and the Netherlands According to the International Trade Bureau, graphite, also known as kyanite, is a carbonaceous mineral. The higher the carbon content, the more valuable it is. Graphite produced in Cumberland, England, contains 92% to 100% carbon and is the best graphite in the world. It is used to manufacture tungsten, antimony, pencils, batteries, paints, stoves, lubricating powders, and is an indispensable raw material in the metallurgical industry. The Netherlands Commercial Visit Bureau sent a letter seeking Chinese graphite miners and exporters for direct negotiations. It is hoped that miners will send a letter to the bureau for introduction.

Germany Needs Tungsten, Antimony, Lead and Tin China's crucible ore production accounts for almost 70% of the world. It has a wide range of industrial uses and is a necessary product for manufacturing munitions. Lead and tin are important raw materials for making lead pipes and tinplate, and are sold in large quantities every year. The German KACRO Company needs a large amount of tungsten seedlings, antimony ash, lead filings, crushed tin, etc. Mineral exporters can send a letter to the company for introduction and sales overseas.

Hanoi and Bangkok Will Have Flights 110

Air France's air service between Hanoi and Bangkok will begin on January 1st next year. The current air service between Malaya and Saigon will continue to be maintained, with Saigon as the terminal. Therefore, Bangkok to Hanoi will be a branch line, which will also be operated with three-engine aircraft. The timetable will be announced later.

The Seafarer Disturbance Expands Merchants Yesterday Decided to Suspend Flights The Chunhe Wheel Was the First Flight to Be Suspended Due to the Customs' Failure to Close the Flight. The Company Is Not Responsible for Passengers and Goods and Appealed to the Departments. 111

According to Xin Sheng, after the Shanghai and Hankou District Seafarer Management Committee announced the seafarer rules, the merchants unanimously opposed them and appealed to the departments. Yesterday, the Shanghai Customs implemented the appointment of seafarers by the Seafarer Management Committee, otherwise it would not be closed. The merchants decided to suspend flights at a general meeting yesterday and notified all passengers to pay attention. The details are as follows:

Implemented Yesterday 112

After the Shanghai and Hankou seafarer rules were announced and implemented on October 1, the merchants strongly opposed them. So far, it has not been resolved. Yesterday, the Shanghai Customs suddenly implemented the new seafarer rules. All ships sailing from Shanghai to the Yangtze River must hire seafarers who have passed the qualification of the Seafarer Management Committee. The seafarer's license issued by the former Navy Department's training school is invalid. The Chunhe of the Hefeng Shipping Company was originally scheduled to sail from Shanghai to Nanjing yesterday. Because the seafarer Yu Ningao, although he held a seafarer's license from the Navy Department's training school, was not a seafarer who had passed the qualification of the Seafarer Management Committee, he was rejected and the flight was not closed, so the Chunhe could not leave the port and was anchored at buoy 27 in the Huangpu River.

Decided to Suspend Flights 113

Related merchants, after receiving the Hefeng Company's report, held an emergency meeting at the Shipping Club on Guangdong Road at 5 p.m. yesterday. More than 30 representatives from Sanbei, Ningshao, Zhengji, Haichang, Zhaoxing, and Hefeng Companies, including Yu Qiaqing, Wang Bofen, Chen Ganqing, Chen Shuntong, and Sun Bingtang, attended. Yu Qiaqing chaired the meeting and reported on the incident of the Chunhe being refused to close the flight. As this matter concerned the vital interests of the merchants, it was unanimously resolved on the spot that the Shanghai Customs must appoint seafarers from the Seafarer Management Committee before both parties have consulted, otherwise the flight will not be closed and the flight will be suspended temporarily. 2. The transportation of passengers and goods to various passengers and goods in the Yangtze River will be postponed. 3. Send a telegram to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Transportation, etc. to petition that the flight must be closed before both parties have held a meeting. 4. Send a letter to the General Customs Office that the flight must not be refused. 5. Notify the various passengers and goods that the goods loaded will inevitably be delayed and delivered, and it will be difficult to take responsibility. The meeting did not end until 7 p.m.

There are more than 120 seafarers in the Shanghai and Hankou District who hold licenses from the Navy Department's Seafarer Training School. Zheng Zenan Discusses Guangdong's Sugar Production Plan 119

Guangdong Province, citing the protection of local industrial products, imposes a 20% import duty on goods from other provinces shipped to Guangdong. Shanghai-made machine-made goods shipped to Guangdong are required to pay supplementary taxes. After the manufacturers reported this to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, it dispatched executive committee member Zheng Zenan to Guangdong to meet with Chen Bonan and explain that promoting domestic goods and protecting industries should be considered from the perspective of the entire nation, and should not focus solely on one region. If Guangdong imposes import duties on domestic goods, and other provinces follow suit, the harm would be unimaginable. After this request, Chen immediately agreed to Zheng's request that goods manufactured by factories established by Chinese nationals would be exempt from import duties in Guangdong. However, this exemption would not apply to goods manufactured by factories established in Shanghai with foreign capital. Zheng stated that in the future, domestic goods shipped to Guangdong with a certificate issued by the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce would be exempt from import duties. Chen agreed to inform the Finance Department to handle the matter accordingly. Zheng also spoke with reporters from this newspaper in detail about Guangdong's sugar production plan, which is well worth recording.

Establishing Sugar Refineries: Guangdong Province is currently implementing a three-year industrial plan, and the sugar manufacturing industry has been brought under provincial management. Zheng visited the provincially run sugar refineries in Guangdong. Currently, there are four refineries. The machinery is supplied by England and Czechoslovakia. To pay for the machinery, 20% of the price is paid upon arrival of the goods, and the remainder is paid in 15 installments after sugar production begins. At the beginning of operations, raw materials were purchased from Java. The provincial authorities have now designated four areas for sugarcane cultivation. The province lends farmers 25 yuan per mu of sugarcane fields. It is estimated that each mu of sugarcane fields requires a cost of 60 yuan from planting to harvest. The provincial authorities now pay farmers 90 yuan per mu of sugarcane, so many farmers are leasing sugarcane fields. Currently, there are over 400,000 mu in the province. There are also over 50 types of sugarcane seeds at the Provincial Agricultural Experiment Station, with excellent growth and development.

Excellent Results: Each mu yields 100 dan of sugarcane. According to experiments, 12 dan of raw sugar can be produced from this. The fuel used in sugar production is sugarcane dregs instead of coal, so the cost is lower. Currently, each dan of raw sugar costs 7.5 yuan for sugarcane and about 1.5 yuan for other expenses. The provincial export tax is 0.7 yuan, so the total cost per dan is 10 yuan. Currently, the provincial sugar from Guangdong sells for 16.5 yuan per dan in Shanghai, so the profit is considerable. According to reports from Guangdong Province, this year alone, the net profit from sugar refining and the control of native sugar production has exceeded 5.6 million yuan. From New Year's Day next year, it is estimated that 800,000 dan can be produced annually. Currently, the southwestern provinces do not use foreign sugar; people have switched to eating sugar produced in Guangdong.

Aggressive Expansion: Chen Jitang also told Zheng that Guangdong Province

Page 11

has had success in the sugar manufacturing industry and is planning an aggressive expansion. The sugarcane planting area will be expanded to five districts. Currently, about 400,000 farmers are engaged in sugarcane cultivation. Next year, the number of sugar refineries will be increased from four to fifteen. At that time, the total annual output can be increased to 3 million dan. It is estimated that the surplus profit will be 16-17 million yuan per year. If this continues, foreign sugar can be completely defeated within five years. Fujian authorities are also proposing to increase sugar production, but the sugarcane planting area in Fujian Province is only in the Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, and Xiamen areas, which is not as large as Guangdong Province.

Current Situation of Foreign Sugar: Zheng also said that at its peak, Java had 175 sugar refineries, producing over 2.4 million tons of raw and refined sugar annually. In recent years, the world's production capacity has gradually recovered. In its largest sales area, sugar refineries have successively closed down. Currently, there are only 45 refineries left. The government has also limited annual production to 500,000 tons. The sugar currently being shipped to China is from the 1932 inventory. The cost of Java sugar is 4.25 Dutch yuan per dan. It is now sold to China for 2.75 Dutch yuan per dan, resulting in a huge loss. Adding the 13.6 yuan import tax, it sells for 19 yuan, leaving no room for profit. Zheng also said that if the central government can keep the import tax on sugar unchanged for a long time, foreign sugar can be eliminated within five or six years.

Funds Still Advanced by the Central Bank

Foreign Rice Similar to Japanese Rice Verified as Tribute Rice 121

2,500 bags of foreign rice, transported from Shandong by the Yu Shun steamer, arrived in Shanghai via Guangdong. After samples were sold in the market, because the rice grains were a mixed of long and round types, with a coarse and white color, resembling Taihu rice, most traders were unwilling to purchase it. However, in order to clarify the source and origin of this foreign rice, the trade association inspected the rice samples and hired rice industry experts to conduct a detailed study. The results showed that the rice was a mixed type of Saigon rice. Therefore, each bag contained both long and round grains. It was determined that this rice must have been purchased from Saigon by Guangdong merchants and then milled in Guangdong rice mills. Since Guangdong did not impose import taxes on foreign rice, it was re-exported to Shanghai for sale. Therefore, 1,500 bags arrived yesterday.

Seeking Chinese Industrialists to Join

Also Willing to Carry Samples to Europe for Promotion

Swedish reporter Bammezi and Swedish pilot Wallender visited the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday to meet with secretary Yan E'sheng. Two Railway Administrations Establish Goods Standard Sample Showroom 123

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, upon the decision of the Goods Standard Freight Rate Research Committee, have established a Goods Standard Sample Showroom at the Shanghai North Railway Station. It is based on the goods obtained by the two railways participating in the National Railway Line Product Exhibition and supplemented by samples solicited from merchants. They are classified and displayed. It has been arranged and will open on November 1st. From 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM on that morning, guests from all walks of life will be invited to visit. The preparation process and the goods that have been collected, as well as the main purpose of the establishment, are described in detail below.

Preparation Process: In August of last year, the Railway Bureau's Goods Standard Freight Rate Research Committee passed a proposal for the establishment of a Goods Standard Sample Showroom, with the location being the Shanghai North Railway Station. Since the facility is closely related to transportation and business operations, the Railway Bureau entrusted the Transportation Department to handle the preparations. In March of this year, the Transportation Department submitted its preparatory opinions, and responsible personnel were immediately assigned to carry out the work. By mid-May, the arrangements had begun to take shape. On June 19th, the original arrangements were deemed unsatisfactory, and an expansion plan was formulated and implemented in an orderly manner. Currently, there are approximately 835 types of goods and 6,208 pieces on display, divided into five major categories: domestic goods, Chinese and foreign goods (with Chinese and foreign products listed side-by-side for comparison), famous products along the railway line, major transportation items of the railway, and special-price items of the railway.

Significance of Establishment: There are two main purposes for the establishment of the showroom: (A) The calculation of freight rates by the railway is based on goods standards. However, there are many types of goods in the world, and Chinese railways are currently only divided into six standards. Whether the items that have been listed are appropriate, how to classify those that have not been listed, and which standard to classify those that are questionable are all problems. Furthermore, the railway authorities are planning to divide the six standards into ten, so it is appropriate to prepare data in advance for reference. However, it is difficult to ensure suitability without knowing the quality, size, and difference of the actual goods. Therefore, it is necessary to collect samples of goods for research on goods standards. (B) The railway's freight transportation is based on the principle of fully utilizing the tonnage of freight trains. However, how to improve packaging to benefit the railway's own business and reduce the freight costs for merchants can only be achieved by observing the actual goods. Therefore, it is necessary to collect samples of goods for research on packaging methods. In addition, there is an ancillary purpose, which is to display the types, quantities, and values of local products for investigation and transport by sellers, in order to develop local resources. It also allows passengers to browse during their waiting time, gaining a deep understanding of domestic goods and encouraging them to purchase them. It is also heard that after the opening of the showroom, there are plans to schedule visits for elementary school students to foster their awareness of protecting domestic goods, and to invite students receiving commercial education to visit for research on commodities.

New Life Movement on the Two Railways 124

Practical Work Already in Progress

Rules and Conventions Announced the Other Day

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways began implementing the New Life Movement early. When the New Life Movement was announced in Nanchang on February 29th, it gave all railway employees a deep understanding of the New Life Movement. Subsequently, on March 24th, the New Life Movement Promotion Association was established by the Railway Administration in conjunction with the Special Party Headquarters. After assigning personnel to make preparations, it was finally decided to formally establish it on August 5th. Because the headquarters had practical work on health and other aspects for the New Life Movement on the railways, on September 3rd, a meeting was convened by the headquarters to reorganize in accordance with the instructions. While this was being implemented, on September 21st, the revised Organizational Outline of the New Life Movement Promotion Association of each railway and the newly revised Organizational Rules of the New Life Movement Service Corps of each railway, issued by the headquarters on September 18th, were received. On October 16th, a meeting was convened to revise the organizational regulations and detailed rules of the New Life Movement Promotion Association of this railway. The director of the Railway Administration, the chief of the Police Department, the director of the Affairs Department, the director of the General Affairs Department, the director of the Mechanical Department, the deputy director of the Engineering Department, and a representative from the Special Party Headquarters served as executive officers. A service corps was established for each of the six sections of the railway: road, car, engineering, mechanical, and police. On the 17th, it was resolved that the first phase of the New Life Convention of the railway would consist of 16 articles. On the 26th, Huang Boqiao (Director of the Railway Administration) was temporarily replaced by Deputy Director Wu, concurrently serving as Weiguo (Director of the Transportation Department), and Li Yuansan (Standing Committee Member of the Special Party Headquarters) were appointed as standing executive officers. The heads of each group of executive officers were also designated, including Jiang Shouzhi for the secretariat group (Chief Secretary), Hu Jizong (Chief of the Personnel Section of the General Affairs Department) for the investigation group, Feng Qili (Engineer of the Su-Song Engineering Section) for the design group, and Ma Shaoping (Chief of the Police Department) for the implementation group. In addition to reporting to the New Life Movement Promotion Association and the Ministry of Railways, the association announced the aforementioned regulations, detailed rules, the list of executive officers for the first phase of the convention, and the list of executive officers for each group on October 30th.

The Board of Directors of the Jin Ting Guild Hall Seeks Relief for the Disaster Victims in Dongting Xishan 126

The Board of Directors of the Jin Ting Guild Hall in Dongting Xishan, Shanghai, has stated that the disaster in their hometown this year is extremely severe and the livelihood of the villagers has been cut off. Yesterday, they sent a special letter to the Shanghai Drought Relief Association, requesting the allocation of funds to relieve the disaster and save the people. The original letter is as follows: We humbly submit that our hometown, Dongting Xishan, which belongs to Wuxian County, Jiangsu Province, is the 13th autonomous region, isolated on Taihu Lake, with simple customs and a population of nearly 40,000. In the past, the people relied on the three major products of rice, fruit trees, and mulberry for their livelihoods. However, in recent years, natural disasters have occurred, and there has been almost no year with a good harvest. For example, the locust plague in the 19th year and the subsequent flood in the 20th year resulted in no grain being harvested. Later, severe cold caused havoc, freezing the lake and killing the fruit trees. In the most prosperous era of mulberry cultivation, the annual income was 500,000 yuan. However, due to the tragic decline of the silk market and the daily decline of prices, coupled with successive years of poor harvests, silkworm farmers have no intention of raising silkworms. To this day, it has fallen drastically, and the harvest is less than one-tenth of what it used to be. The rural economy has already reached an extreme state of recession. Unexpectedly, this year, from summer to autumn, the weather was extremely dry, with no rain at all. Most of the farmland in our hometown is located at the foot of the mountains, making it difficult to draw water. The area that has not been planted accounts for 50-60%. Even the few fields that are relatively low and can be rescued with water are affected by delayed planting, unsuitable climate, and locust damage, resulting in infertile ears. Statistics show that the average harvest in Jinshan is only 15%. As for fruit trees, although there are trees that have not died from the freezing years and are waiting to recover, they are now completely dead due to the effects of drought and cracked soil. No fruit is produced. The lack of goods and price changes is a small matter, but the fruit production that the farmers have cultivated with decades of hard work has suddenly withered, which has a huge impact. In addition, the silkworm production in spring, summer, and autumn was completely unsuccessful, and the price was particularly low. The three major products that the entire mountain relies on for survival have been completely taken away by the weather and the land, with no harvest at all. Such frequent disasters have emptied the granaries. The tragic scene is everywhere. The children are crying for food and cold. How can they continue? Our association is eager to save our hometown, but our hearts and minds are not enough. We have always admired your association's kindness, compassion, and concern. We have no river boundaries. We have already resolved at the sixth standing meeting of our association to publicly elect Directors Xu Jisheng and Xu Huimin and prepare an official letter to come forward and request you to implement benevolence early and distribute righteousness immediately, either by sending staff from your association to the mountain to distribute relief or by allocating relief funds to our association for responsible distribution, so as not to prolong the wait.

The Christain National Salvation Ten Person Group Requests a Ban on Young People Entering Dance Halls 129

Wishes the University Federation to Sincerely Advise Students

Wishes the Authorities to Issue Licenses and Impose Restrictions

Kong Xiangzhao, Wang Zhengyan, Wang Wanbai, Wang Hong, You Shuxun, Shi Youhui, Li Denghui, Zhu Haoran, Shen Weixin, Zhou Zhiyu, Jin Yanqing, Zhu Guishen, Yu Zhiqi, Chen Jinyong, Yao Shiyang, Weng Guoxun, Zhang Zhijiang, Dong Jingan, Zhao Jinqing, Xue Daibi, Xie Songgao, and others, executive committee members of the Shanghai Regional Group of the Chinese Christian Believer's National Salvation Ten-Person Group, wrote to the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession, the Municipal Council of the French Concession, the University Federation, and various universities: We, the Group, uphold the Christian doctrine of faith and action and advocate for national salvation through self-renewal. We have been established for many years. Although our talents and abilities are limited and unable to remedy the difficulties of the times, we are nevertheless outspoken and strive to reverse the decline of customs and the state of society. We cannot remain silent on matters that are harmful to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Based on our humble opinions, we offer our services. We hope that you will understand. Recently, the Standing Committee of our National Executive Committee approved the proposal of Standing Committee members Zhao Jinqing, Li Denghui, and Zhu Guishen to trace back to the Eastward spread of Europe, and dance halls have been established in various parts of our country, especially in Shanghai. In recent years, the world economy has been depressed and all industries have been in decline, but the business of dance halls has developed surprisingly. Although dance halls are a popular activity in Europe and the United States, our country's etiquette and moral education are declining day by day. Young men and women are fascinated by foreign lifestyles and customs, and are flocking to dance. The abuses are truly unbearable. Looking at Shanghai, they are everywhere. Those who enter them display luxury, spending money like dirt. The number of those who run out of money and ruin their families is numerous. Moreover, they spend all night, living in a drunken stupor, wasting time and losing their jobs. Nothing is worse than this. Young students, whose blood and energy are not yet stable, neglect their studies once they enter dance halls. Their spirits become more and more depressed. One wrong step can lead to eternal regret, harming society without end. Young people are increasingly falling into decline. We ask you to advise the students in each university to give priority to their studies and not to set foot in dance halls, so as to avoid decline. We also send letters to the principals of major secondary schools, stating that students who set foot in dance halls should be rejected in the future, so that young students will know what to be vigilant about. On the other hand, we ask the authorities to set appropriate restrictions on the issuance of business licenses for dance halls. Young people who are of school age should not frequent them, so that society can be saved and the country can benefit. Is this appropriate? Please make a public decision. After unanimous resolution, this has been recorded. Therefore, in addition to sending separate letters, this matter concerns the safety and security of society. We hope that you will agree. We have recorded this and respectfully submit it, requesting that you examine and handle it. With our highest regards, we send this to the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession, the Municipal Council of the French Concession, the University Federation, various universities, the Shanghai Regional Group of the Chinese Christian Believer's National Salvation Ten-Person Group.

Ben Niu is a large town belonging to Wujin County, located in the center of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. Its residents live side by side, and commerce is thriving. Recently, the Wudan to Danyang highway was completed, running through the town. Another road to Tongjiang is also being planned, further enhancing transportation convenience. Agricultural products from various ports along the Yangtze River and north of the river converge here, being transported to Shanghai flour mills. Many mills have established purchasing stations here to buy wheat. The Changzhou branch of the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank originally had a warehouse to handle agricultural product storage and mortgage matters. Its business has been extremely flourishing. To better connect towns and villages and facilitate the flow of rural finance, a branch office has been added to conduct remittance, savings, and trust services. Preparations are now complete, and the official opening is scheduled for November 1st. A Survey of National Cultural Institutions Published 135

The China Cooperative Association of the World Cultural Cooperation Society, recognizing the increasing number of cultural institutions in our country but the absence of a comprehensive survey dedicated to them, specially spent a month conducting a widespread investigation. The "Survey of National Cultural Institutions," edited by Mr. Zhuang Wenya, a standing committee member of the association, was published recently. The contents are well-criticized, the printing is excellent, and almost all of the important cultural institutions in the country have been thoroughly collected. The total number is 400, including 43 universities, 39 colleges, 47 specialized schools, normal schools, and people's education centers, 36 research institutions, 14 museums and art galleries, 98 libraries, and 116 cooperative associations, totaling 300,000 words in 600 pages. The general catalog at the beginning of the book is arranged according to the names of the institutions, with the detailed addresses of each institution attached below the name. It is also classified by the nature of the institution, making it extremely convenient to check. In addition, two tables listing the distribution of various universities and colleges and the schools and libraries established in China by foreigners are particularly noteworthy. It is a great work for surveying our country's cultural institutions and an indispensable reference book for the desk. The book is currently sold by the World Book Company at 390 Fuzhou Road, Shanghai, with a list price of two yuan. For the purpose of popularization, it is specially sold at a 40% discount. An additional 7.5 cents for postage and 8 cents for registration are required for out-of-town orders. The number printed is limited, so purchase quickly.

Kidnappers Swallow Ransom Money and Commit Murder 137

Fang Yongmao Deserves Ten Thousand Deaths

Younger Brother Also Involved and Arrested

Zhou Guangyu, a Ningbo native who runs a dried goods store in Lujia Stone Bridge, Nanshi, and his son Sidi were kidnapped without a trace in their hometown in October 1932. Later, the kidnappers sent a letter demanding a ransom. The Zhou family entrusted Fang Yongmao, an acquaintance, to negotiate with the kidnappers repeatedly, eventually agreeing to a ransom of 17,000 yuan. The Zhou family managed to raise 17,000 yuan and handed it over to Fang to go to the bandit's den to redeem the hostages. However, Fang, seeing the money, became greedy and harbored ill intentions. He absconded with the money to Shanghai, hiding at 195 Zhonghua Road. The kidnappers, seeing the negotiations broken off, believed that the Zhou family was not sincere and murdered Zhou Guangyu and his son. The Zhou family, seeing that Fang Yongmao had taken the money to redeem them and had not been heard from for a long time, harbored many suspicions. Later, they received a letter from the kidnappers stating that the hostages had been murdered. Only then did they realize that Fang Yongmao had absconded with the money. After repeated searches, the Zhejiang Security Team finally arrested him in Shanghai this spring and escorted him back to Zhejiang for interrogation. Now, Yu Jishi, Director of the Zhejiang Security Office, found that Fang's younger brother, Fang Yongsheng, was suspected of collusion and deception in the case. Yesterday, he specially prepared a document and sent detectives Hong Yutian and Zhang Shijie to Shanghai, requesting the Yemiao Police Station to send police to assist in the arrest. Chief Liu immediately dispatched Li Sixin to accompany them, and Fang Yongsheng was arrested. After interrogation, he was sent to the General Bureau for further investigation.

Many Lawsuits Involving Longhua Temple 138

The Abbot Xingkong Owes Money

Mediation Fails, Lawsuit Imminent

Since Abbot Guangzhao left the temple and went elsewhere, the Buddhist Council decided to elect a suitable person to take over on December 1st of last year. Venerable Xingkong, from Mount Emei in Sichuan, was introduced as being old, virtuous, and suitable for the role. On the 5th of that month, Xingkong arrived at the temple and took over, discovering that a portion of the temple property, such as the shops in front of the temple, had been leased to Hu Su Ji by the former abbot Yuanzhao, with Hu Su Ji collecting rent. Xingkong then sued Yuanzhao and Hu Su Ji in the Shanghai District Court for colluding to lease the property and infringing on temple property. As a result, Yuanzhao lost the case. Subsequently, Fangcheng, a monk from the temple, accused Xingkong and Chen Shaodan and others in the District Court Prosecutor's Office of coercion and intimidation to publish corrections. As a result, Chen Shaodan was fined 50 yuan. At the same time, Xingkong and Lu Mingzhao from the temple also sued Yuanzhao in the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the court for encroaching on temple property, requesting thorough investigation. The Public Security Bureau arrested Yuanzhao and translated the small leather suitcase (containing all the deeds) and sent it to the District Court. Prosecutor Wu Deying interrogated him and sentenced him to detention pending investigation. It is now learned that Monk Fangcheng recently hired lawyer Peng Bujing to apply to the District Court Mediation Chamber for mediation. The facts are that on the sixth day of the fourth lunar month this year, Abbot Xingkong borrowed 500 yuan from Fangcheng, with two promissory notes (one for 200 yuan and one for 300 yuan). The promissory notes are kept in the Prosecutor Hu Deying's file (because Fangcheng is Yuanzhao's disciple, he stored the promissory notes with his teacher, kept in a small leather box), stating that interest would accrue at a rate of one percent per month and that the money would be repaid in full within two months, with monks Yongchan, Dafen, and Liaoyuan from the temple as guarantors. Because repeated demands were unsuccessful, he had no choice but to pursue legal action. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Zuyu held a hearing for mediation. The applicant, Fangcheng, was represented by lawyer Peng, who stated the previous situation. The opposing party, Xingkong, was absent due to illness, but Yongchan and Dafen attended, stating that Abbot Xingkong did borrow the money, but had paid 50 yuan. Lawyer Peng rose to refute, stating that the 50 yuan was for interest, and the opposing party should pay 500 yuan at once. However, Yongchan insisted on repaying in three installments. Lawyer Peng objected, and the judge ruled that mediation had failed, instructing the applicant to file a formal lawsuit. Longhua Temple is truly troubled.

Funeral Home Clerk Forges Checks and Embezzles Funds 139

Zeng Yanhua Admits Guilt in Court

Court Conducts Preliminary Inquiry

Zeng Yanhua, a Cantonese man, 31 years old, residing at 8, Lane 77, Zhao Jia Bridge, was a clerk and accountant at the Wanguo Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road. Therefore, all money and checks were managed by Zeng. However, according to the funeral home's usual practice, all checks for withdrawals must be co-signed or stamped by the two Westerners, Mr. Seytor and Mr. Brettford. However, the two Westerners could not always be in the same place at the same time. For convenience, Brettford signed the checkbook in advance and gave it to Zeng for management. When a withdrawal was needed, only Seytor's signature was required to withdraw the money. Zeng took advantage of this loophole, imitating Seytor's signature. From May 1st of this year to the end of last month, he forged Seytor's name and stamp on blank check papers and successively collected 2,300 yuan from the Shanghai Citibank, which he used for his own purposes. However, the Wanguo Funeral Home is a company, and every few months, all the books must be submitted to accountant Xue Mailuo for inspection. This time, accountant Xue discovered Zeng Yanhua's fraudulent behavior and reported it to Seytor, who reported it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which issued an arrest warrant from the First Special Court. Zeng was arrested and detained in the police station yesterday. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Chamber of the First Special Court. According to police lawyer Zhang Tianyin, the defendant is accused of forging documents in violation of Article 224 of the Criminal Law. Seytor, the plaintiff, and the Western staff of Xue's accounting firm provided evidence proving everything. The defendant confessed that he was a clerk at the funeral home with a monthly salary of 220 yuan and admitted to forging signatures and embezzling funds. Judge Liu Yugui verified the confession and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody pending further hearing in seven days.

Head Crushed in Machine 140

Iron Factory Apprentice Dies Tragically

Shi Jinhai, an 18-year-old apprentice from Yuyao, who has been working at the Yuhua Xiang Iron Factory at 582 Fair Road for more than three years, was grinding steel rods on a machine tool at around 4:00 PM on the 28th of this month. He was careless and his head was crushed by the machine. He cried for help, and when his companion Zheng Xuedao heard the sound and rushed over, he quickly closed the machine door and tried to get his head out. However, Shi was severely injured at this time. The factory owner and others rushed him to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but to no avail. He died the next morning at 9:00 AM. The hospital reported to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered detective Ji Peijin to investigate. The body was taken to the forensic examination center on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Tang, a prosecutor from the First Special District District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan, clerk Wang Zuqi, and others, arrived at the center to examine the body. Chief Hua Pu Shen Baoshan stated the above situation after examining the body. According to Zheng Xuedao, 22 years old, who testified that he did not witness how Shi's head was crushed by the machine. He only heard the cry for help and rushed over, only to find out what happened and immediately turned off the machine to save him. Shi Guishi, the father of the deceased, 52 years old, testified that he usually works in a pharmacy in Ningbo. He just received the news a few days ago and arrived this morning. He only had one son, and now that this unfortunate thing has happened, he requested that the factory provide compensation. After hearing the testimony, Tang ruled that the deceased Shi Jinhai, male, died from a head injury sustained before his death. The body was released to his father, Shi Guishi, with a written guarantee to take it back for coffin burial and advised the factory to give some compensation to the family of the deceased.
