Customs Patrol Ships Go to Lijiang Port to Combat Smuggling 152

Seizure of a Large Quantity of Tax-Evaded Rayon and Sugar

The Jianghai Customs believes that the residents of Lijiang Port mostly engage in seafaring activities. In this era of developed steamships, there are still twenty-three boat households in the area transporting fish sauce, oil, and other goods to and from Tianjin, Dalian, and other places. However, these boats also carry tax-evaded goods on their return trips, which are then transported inland for sale in Shanghai, Ningbo, and other areas. The amount of such goods is substantial. In order to combat smuggling, the Customs has dispatched two patrol ships, one large and one small, to conduct inspections. The larger ship is stationed outside the port, while the smaller one patrols around the entire island. Any sailing vessel that appears to be heavily laden is boarded and inspected. Yesterday, a small oil tanker fully loaded with rayon and other goods, attempting to smuggle them into Changbai, was seized and towed to Shanghai. At the same time, a sailboat carrying hundreds of bags of sugar was also seized and confiscated.

Measures for Ordering the Replacement of Old Public Rickshaws with New Ones 153

The Public Works Department's Rickshaw Affairs Committee, recognizing that some public rickshaws are dilapidated and unsafe, urgently needs to replace them with new vehicles to ensure passenger safety. On October 19th, a notice was posted at the rickshaw inspection office on Fair Road, stating: "Notice: Hereby notified that any rickshaws deemed dilapidated by the Rickshaw Inspection Office of this Department will be allowed one month to replace them with new vehicles (the style must conform to the new vehicles specified by this Department). Failure to do so within the deadline will result in the revocation of the license by this Committee. Furthermore, the above measures do not apply to vehicles that are severely dilapidated and unusable. This notice is hereby issued for public knowledge."

In the past two weeks, approximately eighty vehicles have been declared as unusable and the owners have been notified by the authorities to replace them with new vehicles within one month in order to continue to obtain licenses. During this one-month period, if the vehicles are adequately repaired, they will be temporarily allowed to be used, but no further extensions will be granted after the deadline. In addition, it has been found that six vehicles are no longer suitable for passengers and cannot be repaired. The owners have been notified that they must provide new vehicles within one month in order to continue to be licensed. During the one-month period, if they wish to temporarily substitute another vehicle, it will be allowed with the consent of the Inspection Office. These measures avoid a temporary reduction in the number of vehicles, which would prevent rickshaw pullers from having vehicles to pull, and it cannot be said that it is difficult for the owners to comply. The Vehicle Committee has always advocated for a gradual approach to replacing vehicles with new models. Existing vehicles that are still usable are allowed to continue to be used.

The Municipal Health Bureau Strictly Deals with Cases of Altering Licenses and Illegally Practicing Medicine 154

The Municipal Health Bureau previously discovered that Chinese medicine practitioner Li Zuolin was falsely claiming to be a physician and illegally operating three Zuolin Western Medicine Hospitals at locations such as Avenue Edward VII in the Public Concession and Avenue Minny in the French Concession. Recently, the Zuolin Hospitals declared that they would be taken over by others. Zhang He had privately erased the name of the foreign doctor Robert Holper (Dr. Robert Holper) on the physician registration license issued by the Municipal Health Bureau and replaced it with his own name. He also replaced the photo on the license. The Municipal Health Bureau considered Zhang He's behavior to be illegal and immediately revoked the altered license to be dealt with according to the law. However, Zhang He dared to go to the Bureau to request the return of the aforementioned license. The English Electric Tram Company Requests Withdrawal of the Violent Ticket Inspection Case 157

The conductor of the No. 416 ticket seller of the public concession tram company in this city, was serving on the 18th Road tram. When the tram arrived at Xieqiao, he was unreasonably beaten and injured by the No. 12 ticket inspector of the French company. This aroused public anger among all the conductors. The Third District Water and Electricity Workers' Union convened a general meeting to discuss solutions and decided to send a letter to the company requesting that it negotiate with the French company to withdraw and punish the violent ticket inspector. They also set a deadline of two days for a reply. Otherwise, when the tram reached the French Concession, they would uniformly stop selling tickets to seek extreme countermeasures. After receiving the letter, the company was deeply concerned that the dispute would escalate, and immediately sent personnel to contact the French company. The French company agreed that the No. 12 ticket inspector would no longer be assigned to serve on English electric trams in order to avoid conflict. If he still engaged in trouble-making behavior, it could be reported and he would be fired immediately. The company authorities then conveyed this intention to the conductors, who were satisfied with the response. Therefore, the dispute has been resolved.

Sweet Words and Malicious Abandonment 159

Money is Deceptively Taken Revealing a Vile Countenance

A Moment of Error Leads to Regret and Irreversible Consequences

Wang Yigong, who used to work as a patrolman in the Huishi Police Station, was dismissed by his superiors for dereliction of duty. He then joined the Tianyunlou Theater of Yong'an Company as an inspector. His family lived at No. 20, Meilefang, Huanlong Road, French Concession. This summer, Sang Zhengbang, a wealthy young man from Changming, brought his beautiful wife Luo Xiuzhen (also known as Luo Yulan), who was close to her prime, to Shanghai for sightseeing. The couple stayed in a hotel. Sang had an opium addiction, and every time he returned to the hotel tired from sightseeing, he would order the waiter to buy opium to satisfy his addiction. One night, the police investigated the hotel and found Sang lying on the couch. He was arrested and taken away. His wife, Luo Xiuzhen, was distressed by her husband's crime and urgently wanted to rescue him. However, she was unfamiliar with the area. She remembered that Qiu was a friend of her husband, so she went to ask for help. Qiu then introduced Zhong Dexin, an inspector at the Tianyunlou Theater, to assist. After several discussions, Luo Yuzhen became acquainted with Wang Yigong through Zhong. Wang saw that Luo was young and beautiful and immediately had inappropriate thoughts. He was very attentive to Luo and learned about her husband's situation. He took the opportunity to slander Sang, saying that Sang did not engage in proper business and only wasted money. He claimed that the family property would inevitably be squandered in the future, and it would be unbearable to spend the rest of her life with such a prodigal son. Xiuzhen already hated Sang for being addicted to opium and being imprisoned in a foreign land. Upon hearing these slanders, she mistakenly believed them to be heartfelt words. Zhong Dexin took the opportunity to encourage her, greatly exaggerating Yigong's handsome appearance and straightforward demeanor. He also said that he was unmarried and that if they could form a love relationship, it would be a good match. Surrounded by these influences, Xiuzhen had no choice but to agree. She immediately took her luggage from the hotel and moved to the home of Wang Yingzhou, the editor of the Tianyunlou newspaper. Yigong and she began an illicit relationship, and then moved to Zhabei. Later, they moved to No. 5, Renhuali, Sapaud Road, as if they were husband and wife. When Sang was released from prison, Luo divorced him and asked Wang to hold the wedding ceremony as soon as possible. However, Wang made excuses. Recently, Wang had taken all of Xiuzhen's property and decided to abandon her. Suddenly, on the night of October 12, he called Xiuzhen to the Great Shanghai Hotel and told her that he had resigned from all his positions in Shanghai and planned to go to another port to make a living. He deliberately talked endlessly, and even stayed overnight. The next day, Xiuzhen returned to the apartment and found that all her belongings were gone. Wang had also disappeared. Xiuzhen realized that she had been deceived. In addition to reporting to the Songshan Road Police Station, she also filed a complaint with the Second Special Court accusing Wang Yigong of obstructing morals, abandoning her, and encroaching on her property. Wang suddenly filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court against Luo Xiuzhen and Zhong Dexin for breach of trust. Yesterday afternoon, both cases were heard simultaneously in the First and Second Courts. However, Luo Xiuzhen had already gone to the Second Special Court, so she could not be present to defend herself against Wang's accusation. Judge Wu Tingqi inquired about the reason and ordered the hearing to be rescheduled to November 8.

More Smuggled Rayon Seized 162

Recently, unscrupulous merchants in this city have been smuggling inferior rayon into the country, evading customs duties, causing the domestic silk industry to suffer a setback. As reported in the newspaper the other day, the customs announced that in the past week, patrolmen seized more than 28,000 parcels of rayon smuggled in the Huangpu River, which is shocking. However, the illicit profits are so great that merchants continue to smuggle in rayon. It is now known that a few days ago, the Shanghai Inspection Office, acting on a tip-off, seized six packages of tax-evaded rayon imported from Guangdong in the Qujiaqiao area of Jiangwan. Yesterday, another 20 boxes of rayon were seized at the North Railway Station. The Customs Department's Anti-Smuggling Section has sent personnel to retrieve the goods and is investigating the owners. According to customs officials, under the new customs law, all seized tax-evaded goods will be confiscated and auctioned off if there is no owner. If there is an owner, in addition to confiscating the goods and turning them into debt, they will be subject to double the penalty.

Zhang Chongxiu Dies from Serious Injuries in a Burglary and Murder Case 164

The Xinjusaigu paper shop at No. 259, Gaoen Road, French Concession, is owned by Zhang Chongxin, a native of Henan. His family lives in the shop. Zhang Chongxiu, Zhang's younger brother, was 31 years old this year and worked as a clerk in the shop. At about 10 p.m. on the 26th of this month, three robbers suddenly came in armed with pistols, and shouted loudly. Zhang Chongxiu, the brother of the shop owner, shouted loudly, angering the robbers. The robbers immediately opened fire as a warning. The bullet hit Chongxiu, in the neck, and he fell to the ground. The robbers stole silver dollars from the cash register and fled. The owner reported the incident to the police station, and the police were strictly ordered to arrest the fleeing robbers. Zhang Chongxiu died from his injuries at 11 p.m. on the 29th, after ineffective treatment. The hospital notified the police station, which transported the body to the forensic examination office of the Tongrenfuyuan sub-hall. Yesterday, the family was notified to report to the case. Wang Ren, the prosecutor of the First Special Court, and the medical secretary arrived at the office for an examination. It was determined that the deceased, Zhang Chongxiu, had died from gunshot wounds sustained during his lifetime. Zhang Chongxin, the elder brother of the deceased, was questioned about the circumstances of the robbery. After that, the body was returned to the elder brother for funeral arrangements, pending the police station's investigation and arrest of the murderers.

Four Banks Reserve Treasury Issues Reserve Report 171

No. 252

The Four Banks Reserve Treasury is jointly established by the Yanzhong, Quan Cheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks to exclusively handle the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the Treasury's issuance regulations, the issuance of banknotes is fully backed by reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and guarantee reserves accounting for at most 40%. A public announcement is made weekly, verified by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The following is a transcription of the Shanghai Reserve Treasury's 252nd announcement on October 27th of the 23rd year. The amount of banknotes in circulation is 29,591,573 yuan. The total amount of reserves is 29,591,573 yuan, including cash reserves of 22,789,323 yuan and guarantee reserves of 6,802,250 yuan.

Meeting Record of the Beijing Road Citizens' Association 172

The 24th District (Beijing Road) branch of the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Zhang Yichen reported that the association was about to send letters to the landlords at the request of the members to reduce rents. It was proposed that the landlords, including Xing Renji, who voluntarily reduce rents should be thanked. It was resolved that separate letters of thanks should be prepared. (1) On the Ministry of Finance's announcement of the new stamp tax law and a request for discussion. It was resolved that: (A) The date of implementation of the new stamp tax, and the old stamp tax will be temporarily kept for exchange, and all members will be notified immediately to comply. (B) The previously set maximum amount of two cents for shipping invoices has been increased to one yuan, a difference of fifty times. (C) For silver and money receipts, a further one cent will be added for every ten yuan. For example, for 10,000 yuan, 10 yuan will need to be affixed. How can merchants bear this heavy burden? For the above two cases, the General Association is requested to forward them to the Legislative Yuan for revision. (2) A joint letter from the Zhong De Li members and others requesting that the Zhong De Company be forwarded a letter to automatically reduce rents to ease the burden. It was resolved that the matter should be forwarded to the company. (3) A letter from the Citizen's Daily Newspaper requesting the promotion of the Citizen's Daily Newspaper. It was resolved that letters should be sent to the members to subscribe. (omitted).

In addition to the unfinished parts of the second volume, which will continue the previous text, there are also rare and isolated copies, such as Yu Quyuan's unpublished poems, Wen Tingshi's Zhiguoxuan Diary, Zheng Wenzhuo's poetry drafts, which are not found in the complete collection, Shen Zengzhi's Hai Ri Lou notes, Wang Yunyun's Extracurricular Essays, Sun Yirang's posthumous works, Wu Dacheng's diary, Chen Yongguang's Qi Yu Yaoweng's unpublished poems, and the recent Chen Sanli's Sanyuan Jingshe Wen Cun still has more than a hundred pieces, which will be fully published in this volume. Wang Jinqing's self-recorded chronicle, which consultants are eager to see, Zhang Xingyan's Gutong Sui Bi, Liang Zhongyi's Yuanju Ge Cuo Tan, Chen Shiyi's poetry talks sequel, Mao Heting's Yunlang Xiaoshi, and Feng Gun poetry case, Xia Jingguan's Rengulou Yuan Kao Qing Shishuo Xinyu, Zhang Yuanji's Series Postscript, Yang Yunshi's Jiangshan Wanli Lou Poetry Collection, and Chen Haoyi's Ti Xiangzhai Talking Past, Retreat Notes, and Essays, three kinds will be published simultaneously, and there are many other famous works. The details are listed in the preview of the main items in the 23rd and 24th issues of the volume. Now the third volume has started. In order to give preferential treatment to regular subscribers, the annual 24 issues, including postage, only cost 5 yuan and 6 jiao for old subscribers and 6 yuan for new subscribers. The general distributor is at No. 161 Wangping Street, this city. There are not many books printed, so all should hurry.

Xin Puyu Hall Minhang Clinic Stops Providing Treatment. Every summer, the Xin Puyu Hall in Shanghai, due to the prevalence of epidemics, specially established a clinic in Puan Hall in Minhang to help the poor and sick, and hired wet nurses to breastfeed the babies in the hall. Now that the autumn season has arrived, it seems unnecessary to establish a clinic again, so the last treatment was held the day before yesterday, and the babies raised were inspected. Free Talk

The Times and Needs 179

— Wu Xiangyu

Who are we writing for? This is indeed a question worth discussing. When we observe this question superficially, it seems very simple, but when we cut this question open and observe it from its cross-section, we feel that this question is not as simple as we imagined, but a multifaceted and complex problem.

When we talk about the question of who we are writing for, we must also talk about what we are writing and how we are writing. In other words, first, what is our writing object; second, what kind of consciousness do we use to write; and third, what kind of skills do we use to write. We know that our society is definitely not the society of thirty years ago, and the tastes of some of our readers are. Although our readers are a very small part, and most people are still outside the circle of our writing influence, we do not deny that their tastes still follow the tastes of people thirty years ago. To be more clear, there are two typical people outside the circle of our writing influence: the first type is relatively the majority, although they have been drained of their blood by imperialism, although they have been shackled to the point of death by feudal forces, their consciousness is still a relic of the pre-historical period, and their lives are still a prototype of the pre-historical period. Naturally, there is no need to talk about those who cannot read among them, and even the minority among the minority, who can read, are at most bookworms—these bookworms are only limited to corroding the original soft Chinese paper-printed books, as for the tough Western paper-printed books, even if they are slightly corroded, they also have some digestion. This is a typical person.

The other type of people, although they also live in cities, their lives are partially or wholly Westernized, or even in contact with genuine red-haired foreigners every day and every hour, and they speak beautiful foreign languages, but the books they read are the worst works among foreigners, either superstitious books or detective movies. This is the influence of he Tara, which is not only contaminated with the mutton smell of foreigners, but also contaminated with the stubborn prejudices of foreigners, and even the whole superstition of foreigners. Therefore, their views are the most vulgar, their consciousness is the most stubborn, they only know foreigners, but do not know China, they only know individuals, but do not know the masses, and this is another typical person.

These two types of typical people who are outside the circle of our writing influence, although their lifestyles are absolutely different, their consciousness has a common point. Both of them do not value pure literary works much, believing that they are outside the classics of sages and worthies. At most, they regard these things as entertainment after tea and wine. Because they think they are entertainment, their standard of choice, from a formal point of view, is that the simpler the better, so chapter novels that tell one thing from beginning to end are most to their liking. From the content point of view, the more superficial the better, so the joys and sorrows of talented scholars and beautiful women are also the most popular themes for them.

When we investigate why these two types of typical people are like this, we can say that their lives determine their consciousness. They live in another world, and the surging thoughts of the world are isolated from them. Although they live in the 20th century, their consciousness is still in the 19th century. The colonial form seen in today's China has its historical reasons and cannot be eliminated in a short period of time.

We see foreign goods all over the Chinese market: we see warships and merchant ships from various countries coming and going in our inland rivers, we see foreign soldiers running rampant in our country, we see foreign hooligans selling drugs and killing people. In other aspects, we see farmers displaced, we see the national industry collapsing, we see the depression in the cities, we see overseas Chinese being oppressed and returning. These intertwined problems and many other problems that cannot be listed are naturally the objects of writing for modern writers. However, using these complex and intertwined modern Chinese social phenomena as the object of writing is definitely not something that people with fossilized consciousness can handle, nor is it something that the most primitive chapter novels in historical evolution can fully perform their functions. To deal with the themes of modern society and make them artistic and active in front of us, we naturally need to adapt to the mainstream of modern thought as its center, and to fully express this center of consciousness, we naturally need the latest skills. However, we can never obtain some inspiration or new forms from the old antiques of Dream of the Red Chamber, Water Margin, and The Scholars. An old dog cannot do new tricks, and this is not a joke. Not long ago, some writers, in order to obtain universal readers, advocated that chapter novels may be adopted within a considerable range. This retrograde policy is not enough to gain a majority of readers, but is enough to hinder the progress of Chinese literature, so that it will never have the hope of success in great works and standing in the literary world. We know that those who advocate adopting chapter novels believe that the reason why new literature is difficult to approach readers is that its form and content are too Westernized. This is actually the trend of the times. In today's era, we can never write the purely Chinese vernacular language of Shi Nai'an, Cao Xueqin, and Wu Jingzi. On the contrary, if Shi Nai'an, Cao Xueqin, and Wu Jingzi were born today, they would probably write modern language like us. Therefore, those who believe that the language in the essays of the Ming Dynasty or The Brave Old Woman is more wonderful than modern language are either deliberately playing the savage or ignorant of the principle of language evolution. The appearance of great literary works will never be achieved overnight, and the acquisition of a majority of readers cannot be achieved by condescension. We must promote the overall cultural progress of society and raise the level of culture, then the number of readers can naturally increase. Therefore, making new literary works readable by the general public is not something that literature itself can achieve alone, nor is it something that can be achieved under the current state. It also requires external forces to promote it. However, gaining a majority of readers is not something to worry about. Chinese literature is a part of the literature of all countries in the world, and China cannot be an exception to the road taken by the literature of all countries in the world. All those things that run counter to the times, their fortresses will eventually be captured by us. Let's wait and see.

Tokyo Correspondence (Part 1) 180

— Zhang Xiangshan

Japanese Literature Notes

During the first half of the year and at the end of the previous year, the much-discussed issues of literary renaissance have vanished without a trace since I returned to Tokyo after summer vacation. Even the literary magazines that served as the main base for the literary renaissance have recently lost their appeal and cannot penetrate the main current of the literary scene. Recalling the glorious history of waving the banner and taking the lead, one can't help but feel the rapid changes in the Japanese literary world.

Recently, the targets of literary debate and the things being promoted can indeed be said to have shifted towards the issue of "conversion" and the revival of subjectivity.

The issue of "conversion" is not limited to the conversion of left-wing writers but also relates to the conversion of the pure literary faction. The central figures of these two factions are, respectively, the young writer Hayashi Fusao and the grand master of pure literature, Kikuchi Kan. The conversion of Hayashi Fusao's faction is, needless to say, a conversion from proletarian literature to conversion literature (this term is not coined by me). The conversion of Kikuchi Kan's faction is a conversion from pure literature to popular literature (or vulgar literature).

Regarding Hayashi Fusao's faction, there are also Takeda Rintaro, Kataoka Teppei, Murayama Tomoyoshi, and others. Their creative theories are in the same direction as Hayashi and Takeda, but others like Tokunaga Sunao and Murayama largely hold different opinions. This is not because of their different wills to convert, but because of their disagreement on art.

The Napp, the Japanese left-wing writers' organization, has been deprived of its excellent theoretical mentor, Hori Tatsuo. Kobayashi Takiji died young one after another, and Miyamoto Kenji also went underground. The remaining leadership, such as Yamada Seizaburo, are mostly old and incompetent. Kajii Motoji was misled by erroneous political dogmatism theories, causing the Napp to stop its brain work. The sound organization collapsed into a state of ruin. As a result, writers felt the lack of theoretical guidance and the destruction of their creative abilities by past political activism. They rose up to criticize the Napp and declared their transformation. The representatives of this faction are Hayashi Fusao, Tokunaga Sunao, Takeda Rintaro, and others.

Hayashi Fusao is a young man with a strong heroic color. He possesses a very strong atmosphere of art-for-art's-sake. When the Napp was overly active and subjective conditions were strong, Hayashi was indeed a good cell that could be overcome. However, once the Napp weakened, this caused Hayashi to reignite the torch of art-for-art's-sake, as if he could no longer be confined by the shackles of hidden principles. This reignition of the torch indeed shocked the Japanese literary world. His theory is that art absolutely cannot be allowed to be used as a utilitarian tool for politics. As for Murayama Tomoyoshi and others, they converted because of the freedom of life, and theoretically still support the past theories. However, regardless of the theoretical differences, they did form a new faction in creative works, which is conversion literature. The subjects of conversion literature are no different from those of pure literature, and the themes are still revolutionary, but they lack activeness and add more psychological analysis. If too little attention is paid to the activeness of the theme, conversion literature can be said to become psychological analysis literature. For example, Murayama Tomoyoshi's *White Night* is regarded as a masterpiece of the conversion faction. At the same time, these weaknesses are fully exposed. However, there are also good points, such as the absence of excessive political atmosphere and standardized, solidified ideologies.

Streets of the South Seas (Part 2) 181

— Hei Ying

Baked by the fierce noonday sun, the smell of asphalt blows with the wind to one's nostrils. That strange smell pierces people's nerves. However, the shirtless and barefoot coolies of Geylang raise their T-shaped hoes and vigorously smash the stones on the street. They don't seem to notice at all and work from sunrise to sunset, without any chance to rest.

(So the smooth roads were built by them.)

Pedestrians all wear hats. In the streets of the South Seas, you can see many different hats: the Dutch hats of European businessmen, the red-topped hats of Malays, the silk-ribboned hats of Turks... Women all like to carry umbrellas. The way those *nyonyas* wear slippers and walk sometimes makes people laugh.

The big-headed Indian policeman, carrying a cross, stands at the crossroads directing traffic. He is most afraid when a bullock cart carrying durians or just a cart of green grass comes from afar. The bullocks walk so slowly that passing a street corner often makes cars and carriages wait for ten or twenty minutes.

At this time, the shops are deserted.

Department stores only let the radio play jazz tunes, which drift to the streets. An American young woman sitting in a rickshaw might think of 42nd Street in New York, where there isn't the best jazz band?

(She suddenly has homesickness.)

Silver light flows in, and it gets dark.

(Part 3)

The closed banks, car companies, bookstores, department stores... are quiet, with only one or two lights flashing inside. The Indian doorman also yawns, lying on the sleeping couch outside the thick glass door, hoping that the city sounds will quickly die down so that he can close his eyelids.

The mixed-race prostitute, who has a Spanish father and a Javanese mother, but they have both disappeared. Leaving the 21-year-old her, she has to go out on the street every night, dodging the eyes of greedy and ill-intentioned policemen and detectives. Sometimes she stands under a street lamp post. Sometimes she wanders on the sidewalk. For the cold of the deep night, she sits down in a coffee shop, smokes an elephant brand cigarette, and sobs.

In the streets of the South Seas, the coffee shop is the last to close its doors. Here, there are young guys from Hainan Island. When it's deserted and there are no customers, he will think of his distant hometown, where there are also coconuts and bananas. And how much his mother is looking forward to his return, but....

The unemployed man walks on the street, he has no home tonight. A sigh that fell from the edge of life adds a layer of thick coolness to the night air.

(Where to rest?)

Wandering, street after street...

The night is long, and he doesn't know how much further he has to walk before dawn.

Selling Chrysanthemums 182

— TK

Small Square (Six) 183

— Wei He

I listened to these words as if deaf and mute, gnashing my teeth in pain, a feeling of humiliation piercing deep into my lungs. It was as if I were a little monkey, and my father were a quack doctor outside a theatre, shamelessly selling my little skills, flattering the guests and asking for money, while I myself played a ridiculous role in the midst of loud gongs and drums.

Those round-faced gentlemen gathered closely around the square table on which I was writing. I wrote with difficulty, but they shouted enthusiastically. Criticizing this way and pointing out that way, sometimes they nodded their fat pig-like heads together and stomped their feet and cheered in unison.

The father, holding the paper, was clearly overwhelmed with joy. This could be seen from his trembling hands and excited tone.

The strokes must be forceful, and you can't relax even a little bit. Ah, that's right...

He constantly winked at those people, smiling contentedly. The mother, standing to the side, also followed with a blank smile. The more pleased they were, the more resentment I felt, the more disappointed I felt, always hanging my head. It was fine at first, but later I felt my hands stiffen, my eyes blur, my waist ache, my feet cold, and my whole body convulsed as if trembling.

Look how little is biting her teeth, not even smiling once, she's really got some energy!

These teasing words made me completely unbearable. Perhaps to vent my anger, I suddenly decided not to write the couplet designated by my father, but instead used a couplet that I had thought of myself. At that time, my heart was beating extremely violently, as if all the blood vessels in my body were surging with a tide of anger.

"Red Gate—"

I quickly wrote these two words. The father quickly searched within the couplet he had designated, but there was no couplet that started like this, which made him anxious.

Page 14

Education News

Ai Xianzhou's Test of Ten Thousand People Shows That the English Level of College Freshmen is Only Equivalent to American Junior High School Sophomores 184

For Educational Convenience, Universities and Middle Schools Should Not Use English Textbooks

The Education Experiment Institute of the Education College of Central University, entrusted by the China Education and Culture Foundation, conducted a survey to improve English teaching, presided over by Ai Xianzhou and Zhang Shiyi. Since receiving the commission, Ai has gone to famous universities and high schools in the north and south provinces twice, in May 21 and May of this year, to conduct tests. The students tested were nearly 10,000. Now that the preliminary statistical work has been completed and the problem of analysis and research is being addressed, various detailed tables and charts have been prepared in advance. They compare the English reading fluency and comprehension performance of university and high school (part) students, as well as comparisons with American students. The following lists the important facts shown in each table and their causes: 1. Inland universities (such as certain provincial universities) and normal colleges (such as a certain provincial women's normal college) have the worst results. The reasons seem to be due to inconvenient inland transportation and poor middle school teachers. Students of normal colleges come from normal schools, and the English in normal schools has long been listed as an elective course, so the level is fundamentally uneven. 2. In terms of the four types of universities: national, provincial, private, and church-run, the national ones are better than the provincial ones, and the church-run ones are better than the national ones. This is because church universities pay special attention to English. Private schools located in commercial ports also have not weak results. 3. The results measured this year are better than those measured two years ago. There are two reasons that can be inferred: one is that in the year of the September 18th Incident, students in various schools were often absent from class, so their results were worse; the other is that in the past two years, the Chinese middle school entrance examination system has been implemented. High school graduates with considerable English proficiency are not easy to get into universities. 4. Comparing the results obtained from the two tests with the results obtained from the same tests in American middle schools, the difference is very large. The best English comprehension and speed level of our university freshmen is only equivalent to that of American junior high school sophomores. Moreover, the test period was in May, while the test period in American middle schools was in November. Compared with the two, there is still doubt. Now Ai has sent a letter to Mr. Stone in the United States to investigate. If our college students study for a full year, and their average score is only equal to that of American students who have just entered the first year of junior high school, then the distance between the two will be even greater. Based on the conclusions derived from the above points, Ai believes that to improve the English level of our universities and middle schools, we should improve the English teachers. After all, the poor results of inland students and the poor teachers should bear major responsibility. However, the effect of this method is limited. After all, it is difficult for students to make progress by leaps and bounds. It can be predicted. Therefore, for the convenience of teaching, we should fundamentally advocate the translation of books, and middle schools should not use English textbooks, and many reference books should also use translated versions, because Chinese people read Chinese books more conveniently. It is hoped that those who run universities and middle schools across the country will pay attention to it. According to the Central University Education College's recent publication of the *Education Series* Volume 1, Issue 2, which publishes many research results of the Experiment Institute, the main points are explored as follows: The Mission of the Education Experiment Institute (Ai Wei), Several Attempts of Industrial Psychology Technology (Du Zuozhou), Mental Hygiene of Problem Children (Wu Nanxuan), The Needs and Training of Vocational Teachers (Zhong Daozan), John Muller's Special Nerve Ability Theory (Pan Shu), A Brief Account of the Chicago Education Survey (Xia Chengfeng), Comparative Research on Chinese and American Intelligence (Wang Shulin), The Development of Industrial Psychology in Various Countries (Xiao Xiaorong), Mr. Bartler and His Recent Works (Ai Wei), The Transformation of European Aesthetic Education Thoughts (Chen Zifo), Art of Rome (Li Jiazi), Application Problems in Elementary School Arithmetic (Zhao Tingwei), and Funding Issues for University Libraries (Gui Zhigen).

Xu Guanyu

To Study Scout Administrative Work in the United States 189

Dai Shoutao, vice president of the Chinese Boy Scout Association, and Zhu Jiahua and Zhang Zhizhong, deputy directors of the Preparatory Office, previously requested the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang to send Secretary Xu Guanyu to the Boy Scouts of America to study administrative work, participate in national leadership training, and investigate the general situation of Boy Scouts in various places. The Central Committee has now approved it, and the United States has been informed in advance and expressed its welcome.

Jiaxing Education Funds Cause Panic

The funds for primary and secondary schools in Jiaxing County are mainly derived from county taxes. However, due to the drought and disaster this year, the income from land taxes has decreased, resulting in a significant reduction in the educational funds derived from county tax revenue. Although the education authorities have tried their best to plan, all funds are designated for specific purposes and cannot be diverted for long. Therefore, the regular expenses issued to various schools cannot be met, and the accumulated arrears have reached six months. The principals of each school have repeatedly demanded the money, but there is no solution. The principals of each school believe that it is inappropriate for teachers to teach on empty stomachs, and they have recently requested the education authorities to find a way to maintain the situation. If there is no solution by November 16, they will stop teaching and seek other livelihoods. Therefore, the director of the Education Bureau is discussing with the administrative authorities to maintain education so that each teacher can concentrate on education.

Jinan University to

Prepare for the Memorial Service for Li Shicen 190

Professor Li Shicen of National Jinan University was a highly respected master of philosophy in China. Unfortunately, he died of illness in Jinan New Village the day before yesterday. The teachers and students of the school suddenly lost a good teacher and friend and have been in great grief for days. President Shen Pengfei recently appointed Zhang Yaoxiang, Guo Yicen, Lu Shaozhong, Xia Yande, Chen Ruzhou, Li Qirong, Zhou Guangzhong, and Yang Shusun to form the Preparatory Committee for Li's Memorial Service. The second meeting was held in the conference room at 4:00 pm that afternoon. All nine people attended, chaired by Zhang Yaoxiang and recorded by Xia Yande. The following duties were assigned: General Affairs: Zhang Yaoxiang and Chen Ruzhou; Communication: Li Qiluan and Li Xianshi; Documents: Yang Shusun and Zhou Guangzhong; Publication: Guo Yicen and Xia Yande; Affairs: Lu Shaozhong and Ni Xiusheng. It was decided to solicit many items and select a location to start work on a specific date. It is reported that a grand memorial service has been scheduled for November 9 (Friday) at 9:00 am in the school's Zhiyuan Hall. All institutions, schools, newspapers, organizations, Li's relatives and friends, and those who admire Li's academic and personality are welcome to attend. If you have any items to send, you can send them to the General Affairs Section of the University from now on. Li was well-versed in Chinese and Western learning during his lifetime, lectured in the north and south, had extensive social interactions, and his students were like clouds. His posthumous honor will be a grand occasion at that time. In terms of publication, in addition to the special issues published by various newspapers in Shanghai, the association is also preparing to publish a special issue of the *Education Magazine* and is starting to compile a large book, *Li's Commemorative Album*. His posthumous photos, posthumous works, posthumous records, and commemorative articles from all walks of life are being collected these days. They are also hoped to be sent to the association so that they can be included together. The deadline for collection is set for one month.

City Education Bureau

Allocates Funds to Treat Children with Tuberculosis 191

Some Children Have Shown Improvement

The City Education Bureau pays great attention to weak children. Since Dr. Gao Jinglang was invited to hold a tuberculosis injection test last year, all those suffering from tuberculosis have been rescued in every possible way, despite the lack of funds. For example, in October of the 22nd year, Peter Elementary School held a tuberculosis injection test and divided the reactive children into four categories: (A), (B), (C), and (D). All disposal measures were published in the newspapers in January of this year. Now, the following explores the situation of children with tuberculosis receiving treatment in the second semester of the 22nd year: 1. Three children in category A were sent to the hospital for treatment. Except for one who is still hospitalized, the other two have been discharged from the hospital. 2. Children in category B are practicing half-day reading and half-day rest. The rest place is in the surplus room of Dehua Elementary School. Nurses from the South Shanghai Health Office are sent to the school every afternoon to take care of them. They also take cod liver oil every day and are sent to the First Hospital of the Chinese Red Cross Society for examination once a week. 3. In addition to taking cod liver oil every day, children in both categories are sent to the Red Cross Hospital for examination every four weeks. 4. Statistics at the end of the semester show that: 1. 180 people were examined for the first time, 2. 41 people were classified into category B, 3. 2 people in category B and 12 people in category C were unwilling to go to the hospital for treatment again, 4. A total of 125 people were treated in the hospital, including 7 entering category D, 61 progressing, 49 without progress, 5 more serious, and 3 questionable. At the beginning of the academic year, the school continued to hold treatment for children with tuberculosis. There are currently 54 children who should read for half a day and rest for half a day. Although most children can barely read all day, 8 of them and the 5 more serious ones in the statistics at the end of the school year must be given appropriate rest. The City Education Bureau allocates 50 yuan per month for the children's resting place, and will gradually improve hygiene facilities by setting up a bathroom.

— Sun Yucai

Furthermore, in terms of education and culture, people of all countries harbor negative feelings towards Japan. The gunfire of September 18th and January 28th shocked the world. Countries referred to Japan as the second Germany, calling it an aggressive imperialist or a barbarian state. However, most people did not pay much attention to Japan's cultural situation. Representatives from various countries will only see the advantages of Japan and will not see its disadvantages. Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 210

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 4: A Cup of Water Reveals Hardship, A Bureaucrat Protects the Elderly, Ten Thousand Gold Coins Discuss Mountains, A Cunning Official Imitates

Poor people, seeing rich people enjoying all kinds of benefits, always harbor resentment, thinking that since everyone is human, why do some suffer so much while others enjoy so much? However, once they have dealings with rich people, they are very willing to have a close relationship with them, hoping to get some help from them. In Hu's eyes, Cheng Zhiqian was always a top-class rich man. Because he went to Little Western Paradise every day, and always saw him associating with friends who rode in cars, that was clear evidence. Because in Xi'an city, there were no privately owned cars. Even the cars of merchants were those large trucks and long-distance buses. The sedan-style cars that came and went on the street were no more than a dozen or twenty, and those were all from the various government offices. So in Hu's eyes, all the people who rode in sedan cars on the street were "老爷 (Lǎoyé)" masters. This assumption of hers cannot be said to be wrong. And because Zhiqian was always with these people, naturally he was also a quasi-"老爷". Now that she had brought Zhiqian home, she very much wanted to establish a close relationship with him, to sell Yueying to him as a concubine. Unexpectedly, his first reply was that this was not the solution. Hu, in the backyard of Little Western Paradise, had secretly noticed that Zhiqian had sneaked several glances at Qieying, seemingly he also cherished this little girl, now that she had brought him home, could there be any change of heart? So she leaned against the yellow earthen wall, hooked her small feet, grabbed the copper ear pick on her bun, and kept scratching in her hair. Smiling, she asked: "老爷, we poor people have few ideas, do you have any other solutions?" (53)

Wang Renqiu's Discourse on Emotion 211

— Yanqiao

Wang Renqiu had an interesting view on the issue of emotion. He said that love between two people is not limited by age. Emperor Xuanzong of Tang and Yang Guifei were hardly fond of the young; Empress Wu's "controlling cranes" was also as if she forgot her age. So he, at the age of eighty, was still fond of Zhou Ma. He also said; Li Changji said, "If heaven has emotions, heaven would age," but he did not know that emotion's aging is irrelevant. Emotion naturally arises from blood and qi, without blood and qi there is no emotion, and where can one see nature by exhausting emotion? The Song people mistakenly thought that nature and emotion were evil, but they did not know that good and evil are both emotion, and Dao is also emotion. Blood and qi are nature, and food and sex are walls, so fish see Xishi and dive deep, and Qiang Shi sees fish and wants to net and hook, each using their emotions. Peeping at walls is not allowed, and piles and scabies do not involve emotion. It is precisely a matter of course. Are literary men's jests really arguments? Empress Wu's controlling cranes is similar to Deng Tu's lust, but controlling cranes is not her match. This is Empress Wu's misfortune, she directly indulged her nature without using emotion. All in all, we know that Xunzi's theory of the evil nature of man is better than Mencius's theory of the good nature of man. Mencius only talked about habit. This theory is quite in line with the modern change of accepting the sacred. The Song Confucians only worked hard and spent ink on the two things of nature and heart, but never thought of an emotion. Confucius said that food and sex are nature, but Renqiu insisted that it is emotion, Renqiu wants to justify himself with this. However, there is inevitably some far-fetchedness. However, people now always combine the two words "性情 (xìngqíng)" nature and emotion into one conversation, then nature is emotion, and emotion is nature, one and two, two and one. The nature said by the Song Confucians can also be extended to the word emotion, and in this way, Renqiu's words have no place to refute.

Like the relationship between Qian Muzhai and Liu Rushi, Renqiu's theory of emotion can of course be used to prove it, so Liu Rushi said, "My hair is his face, my face is his hair." As for Renqiu saying: Empress Wu's controlling cranes is similar to Deng Tu's lust, it is indulging nature without using emotion. It seems to contradict itself, above it has already been said that he forgot his age, of course it is born from the word emotion. Song Yu peeping at the wall is of course unrequited love. But Pan Boyin once wrote in the ancient capital, "The one who peeks at the wall for three years shoots Tang: always the Yuguan (Jade Gate) is emotional," so what is unrequited love, a one-sided emotion, if not emotion?

Renqiu is a Han scholar, so he is opposed to the Song Confucians. The conclusion also leads to a debate on the good and evil of human nature, but he has developed a theory of emotion on Yang Yuhuan and Wu Zetian that other scholars would never have the courage and wit to do.

Snippets 212

In the past, people wore clothes for several mornings; now, clothing changes several times a year, even several times a season. So now people's marriages also involve marrying several times in a lifetime, and marrying several times a year!

Old clothes can be renewed; I don't know how people change, and how they will be dealt with when they get old? I really have to worry a lot for them!

Tiger Mountain Marvels 213

— Fufan

A few days ago, I went to a hostel to visit my friend Mr. Liu from Xuzhou, and saw that he had a poem that said: "Tiger Mountain is full of treasures, wind and rain confuse Xuzhou." I asked him about it. Mr. Liu said: "South of my hometown city is a mountain called Tiger Mountain, with beautiful scenery and hidden marvels. Yang Yingquan wrote about it, a famous figure in the Qing Dynasty Qianlong period, who loved books and writing, and was famous in Jiangbei. He served as prefect of Jiangzhou for ten years, and all his income was used to buy antiques; soon he witnessed the filth of the Qing court, so he resigned and returned to seclusion. He carved the ink treasures he had collected over the decades into stone, and built them into surrounding walls, with covered corridors above to protect them from wind and rain; he also established a poetry society, alternating in singing and harmonizing. For a time, Tiger Mountain became a gathering place for Jiangzhe literati. The ancient sites of the wall consist of the Eight Views of Pengcheng, Su Dongpo's Before and After Chibi Rhapsody, Mi Nan Gong's writings, Song Yue's Before and After Master's Table, and Zhu Yuanzhang, Dong Qichang, Zhu Xi, Deng Wenyuan, Tang Yin, Huang Tingjian, and Wang Xianzhi's inscriptions, prefaces, lyrics, and rhapsodies, totaling more than a hundred kinds, which are treasures of the world. A certain greedy official in the Qing Dynasty learned that Yang had these rare treasures hidden, and once sent someone to say that these antiques must be returned to the Great Interior. Yang bribed the visitor with a large sum of money, saying that the antiques were fake, and only then was he spared. Later, when the Red Sheep Rebellion arose, Xuzhou bore the brunt, and flames of war spread everywhere. The ancient precious steles were buried in weeds and desolate smoke, and the wind and rain eroded them, which is very regrettable." Mr. Liu then took out more than a hundred kinds of rubbings from his leather box for me to see. I felt that they were dazzling, antique, elegant, majestic, and complete, truly a thousand-year-old wonder!

Symphony of Literary and Martial 214

— Shiying

Records of Incense Vaguely Heard 215

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

In fact, we also understand very well that prohibitions are always observed only on the surface; secretly, I don't know how many thousands of eyes are hiding in suitable places, boldly, not hesitating to test the law!

Finally, we arrived in front of the palace: the entire team stopped outside the official gate. Once here, we inevitably had to pick one of the prescribed rituals to perform. First, we must not let the Empress Dowager walk in alone coldly: because in the Qing Palace, there is a very stubborn habit - in fact, all the habits in the palace are simply stubborn without exception - whenever the Emperor or Empress Dowager deigns to visit a place that is not often visited, someone must first line up and kneel to greet them inside before it can be considered dignified. This is the situation now. So that chief eunuch Li Lianying became greatly flustered: whenever it was time to perform a ritual, we couldn't help but ask him to be the director, and naturally he was indispensable at this moment. He first gave a wink to the sixteen young eunuchs carrying the Empress Dowager's phoenix palanquin, and they knew it, immediately stopped moving forward, and stood upright in the center of the imperial road, so that the Empress Dowager's face was exactly facing the largest door in the middle of the three-affiliated palace gates.

These sixteen eunuchs stood like sixteen stone statues, shouldering the Empress Dowager's phoenix palanquin, motionless: because this phoenix palanquin must absolutely not be allowed to touch the soil, otherwise, in ordinary people's official sedan chairs, when the owner sits upright inside waiting for something, the sedan chair carriers can temporarily unload the burden on their shoulders, let the sedan chair stop on the road, and the owner is generally very comfortable, and they are much less tired. However, this kind of blessing is not something that the sixteen young eunuchs carrying the Empress Dowager's phoenix palanquin dare to imagine: at this time, not only can they not put the palanquin down on their shoulders to rest, but they don't even dare to pant loudly! (163)

Various Calls 216

— Yiyi Pavilion Master

The various calls mentioned here are the various terms of address. Terms of address in our China are diverse and endless. Now, I might as well write down what I know for you to see.

For example: Grandfather, some places call him "爹爹 (diēdiē)"; some places call him "爷爷 (yéyé)"; and some places call him "公公 (gōnggōng)".

For example: Grandmother, some places call her "娘姆 (niángmǔ)"; some places call her "娘娘 (niángniáng)"; and some places call her "奶奶 (nǎinai)".

For example: Father, some places call him "爷 (yé)"; or "爷爷 (yéyé)": some places call him "爹 (diē)"; or "爹爹 (diēdiē)": and some places call him "伯 (bó)"; or "阿伯 (ābó)"; and some places call him "爸爸 (bàba)"; or "伯爷 (bóyé)".

For example; Mother, some places call her "姆妈 (mǔma)"; some places call her "妈妈 (māma)"; and some places call her "娘 (niáng)"; and some places call her "阿妈 (āmā)".

Okay, okay, just this point alone, the various calls, I think it is enough to make the readers dizzy! If we were to write out all the various dialects and local languages of the provinces and counties (in fact, there are many local words that cannot be written), this publication would certainly not have such a large space to accommodate them, and even the readers would have a headache from it! Alas! All in all, the complexity of Chinese dialects can be imagined simply by looking at the various calls listed above! Then what's so strange about some people wanting to use English to replace the various dialects and local languages of the provinces and counties to communicate? Alas! From this point of view, unifying language and promoting the national language are really urgent matters!

Small Gardening

Pomelos and Chestnuts 217

— Zheng Yimei

(I) Pomelos

Among autumn fruits, the largest are pomelos. The tree is a perennial evergreen shrub, produced in Fujian and Guangdong. The trunk is over ten feet tall, with thorns on the branches. The leaves are long and oval, and the petioles have small, membranous appendages. The fruit is four or five inches in diameter, round, and light yellow. The skin is very thick and difficult to peel. There are many varieties; those with white flesh and a sweet taste were anciently called "aromatic medicine." Some say: the ones with light red flesh inside the skin are called "aromatic luan," and those with white flesh and light crimson are called "zhuluan." Pomelos from Zhangzhou are the most famous. The Zhangzhou Prefectural Records state: "The best persimmons are called pomelos, produced in Changtai County, with a white color and a clear, fragrant taste, pleasing in their elegance. Only those grown in Xidong are superior. Not much is grown in that area, and they are not as good when transplanted elsewhere." Additionally, the Shatianyous from Rong County, Guangxi, are especially famous throughout the country. In Jiangsu and Zhejiang, sour pomelos are called "pao," while in Fujian, all pomelos are called "pao," also written as "pao." Those produced in Siam are smaller in shape and darker in color, seemingly unworthy, but the juice is dense, sweet, and fragrant, making them of the highest quality. As the ancients said, "Judging a person by appearances can lose you a great scholar," which is especially true in this case.

The flowers bloom in late spring, with round, white stamens like large pearls. When they open, they resemble camellias, with a very clear fragrance, similar to jasmine. Foreigners pick them to steam for fragrance, with a superior flavor. See Fan Chengda's "Gui Hai Chu Heng Zhi."

When choosing pomelos, those with a high top and fine lines are best; those that are flat and round with coarse lines are sure to be sour. If the peel is intact when peeled, it can be dried in the sun, and its shape resembles a bowl, which can be used to store things. In the past, it was an essential item for old people who smoked dry tobacco. Pomelos have seeds inside. When soaked in water, they become exceptionally sticky, and women used them to apply to snow creams, but its uses are not as ubiquitous as the ephemerality of udumbara flowers.

There's an interesting anecdote about pomelos. I recall one year when I wrote a New Year's Day article for a certain publication, but the printer mistakenly printed "New Year's Day" as "pomelo." The next day, the editor, Mr. Wu, sent me a note saying: "I gave you New Year's Day, and you returned a pomelo. It's not a reward, but a punchline." Quoting from an opera, it was quite amusing.

Senior Wang Xishen once wrote a small treatise on aromatic luan, saying: "Its fragrance grows stronger as it travels further. Quietly facing it in a bright window is like being in a fragrant orchid pavilion, like meeting ancient poets. Its taste is like a sip of fine wine, not needing to be awakened by strong wine, it naturally intoxicates with its mellow aroma. There are many famous products among the fruits and vegetables of China, but if you want to seek one with profound depth, you must promote this 'gentleman' as a great fruit. Even those rare flowers, jade herbs, and fresh fruits that come from distant sea voyages often excel in being plump and heavy, but none can compare with this one." With such praise, the pomelo is undoubtedly worthy of it.

(II) Chestnuts

Among fruits, chestnuts are originally a top choice. Lu Qiong listed them alongside jujubes and hazelnuts, and traveling with water caltrop and gorgon fruit. They belong to deciduous trees, with trunks four or five zhang tall. The leaves are like simple blades. They bloom in early summer, and after the flowers fall, they are collected and burned; they do not extinguish even in wind and rain. The fruit has a large, spiky burr like a hedgehog. They ripen after the frost falls. The outer shell is hard, dark purple, and contains one, two, or three or four nuts inside, with pale red kernels that are edible. There are also those with one small fruit per burr, which are the original species of chestnut, called "lie." Their fruit is called "zhuli," mistakenly written as "maoli," commonly called "acorn."

Osmanthus chestnuts are produced on the shores of West Lake in Hangzhou, in Manjuelong. Chewing them naturally imparts the fragrance of osmanthus chestnuts, as the area is full of osmanthus, and the flowers' fragrance permeates them. There are also such things in the countryside of Liangxi, with a fragrance no less than those produced in Manjuelong, but their name is not as well-known.

The method of planting chestnuts is to bury the seeds in moist soil in late winter or early spring, planting them in a sunny place. Wait for them to grow several feet before transplanting them. At the vernal equinox, graft them onto oak trees or the most robust of the chestnut trees themselves. They are afraid of the cold, so wrap them in straw in early winter and remove it in the second month.

Some chestnuts are extremely large. The "Book of Later Han, Biography of Ma Han" states: "Ma Han produces large chestnuts like pears." Lu You jokingly wrote: "Frost chestnuts as big as fists." The "Poetry Meaning Notes" states: "Guiyang has clusters of chestnuts, as big as persimmons." Zheng Zhong's Records state: "Zhengzhong produces giant chestnuts, saying that their shells can be used as cups." As for the "Shen Yi Jing" which says: "In the eastern wilderness, there is a tree named 'eye chestnut,' whose shell is three feet and three inches in diameter, with thorns over ten feet long, and the fruit is three feet in diameter," it is absurd and unreasonable and cannot be believed.

The ancients wrote many famous lines about chestnuts, such as Geng Xin saying: "Autumn forests have fatter chestnuts." Fang Hui said: "All yellow, new chestnuts are tender." Du Fu said: "Mountain homes steam chestnuts warm." Fat, tender, warm—these capture the essence of chestnuts, which only a seasoned foodie would know.

Chestnuts are best cooked with candy or stir-fried with sand, which makes them sweeter and more palatable. Recently, some have used machines, without manual labor, to stir-fry them with honey, making them even more exquisite.

Process of Yarn and Cotton Futures Delivery 223

6,400 Bales of Yarn at a Price of 178 Yuan

10,500 Loads of Cotton at a Price of 35.5 Yuan

The October period standard yarn was auctioned on the morning of May 1 this year. The price of the first lot was 174.1 yuan, which fell to 3.7 yuan. The factories, due to high cotton prices and sluggish yarn markets, reduced production in order to maintain survival. Before long, in the North China area, the price of Japanese coarse yarn was higher than that of Chinese yarn, and Tianjin and other places came to Shanghai to purchase Chinese yarn in large quantities. Therefore, people's hearts were greatly excited, and the market gradually turned around, resulting in a reduction in inventory and the market price rising from this point. Later, in mid-June and July, the weather was extremely dry, and cotton prices tended to rise. At the same time, there was a sharp rise in wheat and flour, and the financial community made huge profits. The standard yarn was also purchased in large quantities, and the standard highest price was once seen at 188.8 yuan. However, due to the high price and slow sales, rampant banditry in Sichuan, a remittance of 1,500 yuan, strange growth in silver prices, falling gold prices, and low-priced calculations of three-product yarn, the Japanese dumped a lot of money, and the pressure was particularly heavy. And there were old yarns arriving, and the recipients were lacking, and the market suddenly turned down, breaking from 80 yuan to the 170 yuan mark, and the lowest was once seen at 168.5 yuan. Until October 15, the National Government increased the export tax on silver and added a balance tax, and the foreign exchange shrank strangely, and the gold price soared, and the prices soared. On the 18th, the standard yarn had a momentary frenzy, and the highest price was seen at 183.9 yuan. Before long, the gold price fell back, and the market slackened, falling again to 175 yuan. As a result, the remaining 6,400 bales were delivered at a price of 178 yuan, including 400 bales of Fuguis and 400 bales of Qiuhe for new goods, and the rest were old goods. The brokers and numbers of the receiving and delivering parties are listed below.

The October period standard cotton was auctioned at the opening of the market on May 1 this year. The price of the first lot was 32.65 yuan. At this time, the psychology of most people was that the arable land had greatly increased this year, because the rice price was too cheap last year, and farmers had mostly switched to planting cotton trees, which had thicker harvests, so the throwers were quite turbulent, but slightly fell to 2.35 yuan. Before long, Chenhua 6, 7, and the Dan period were thin on the bottom, and the foreign cotton was stable, and speculators absorbed a lot, and later the American drought and the reduction of arable land under the Peng Haide Act, and the domestic climate was dry, and the drought was severe, and the development of cotton was greatly damaged. , the market price rose from 33 yuan to 36.7 yuan, and the highest was once reached 37.35 yuan. It was spied that the government report on August 8 was beneficial to the long, but the domestic yarn sales were not smooth, and there were large sales by large households, and the parcel amount was more than 100,000 loads. The market was suppressed by it. On October 15, the China Cotton Production Improvement Association reported that the acreage had increased, and although the drought was severe, the output was still 1 to 2 million loads higher than the previous year. The heart turned soft again, and the lowest was still 33.55 yuan. Until October 15, after the National Government increased the export tax on silver and added a balance tax, the cotton market jumped wildly, and the highest was once seen at 37.1 yuan. Grain Spot Prices of Foreign Wheat are Decreasing, Futures Prices of Flour and Wheat are Gradually Declining 226

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for each month continued to show a weakening trend. In terms of foreign wheat quotations, Chicago fell 34 cents in the near term and 90 cents in the long term, while Canada fell about 20 cents. When the opening price was quoted, market sentiment was uneasy due to changes in foreign wheat prices. The opening price for this month was as low as 40.05 cents, a significant drop of 8 cents compared to the previous day's opening price. The prices for the long-term months also dropped by 23 cents. However, after the second round of trading, some shorts covered their positions for profit, and some outsiders also competed to buy, so the market rebounded, rising by 34 cents compared to the opening price. When the market opened in the afternoon, prices fell across the board. The spot price of foreign wheat was even lower. A vessel was indeed traded at 4.96 yuan the day before yesterday, but yesterday only 4.70 yuan was offered. Factories were only willing to pay 4.85 yuan. With this news in the market, selling pressure naturally increased, and prices gradually declined. The eager sale of foreign wheat and the determination of factories to purchase it are obstacles to the market's future. As a result, the price for this month fell 1.5 cents, November fell 1.75 cents, December fell 1.25 cents, January-February fell 2.25 cents, and March fell 2.5 cents.

After the opening of the wheat market in the morning and afternoon, prices for each month fluctuated in a flat and weak manner. In terms of foreign wheat quotations, Chicago fell slightly, from 34 cents to 90 cents, while Canada fell slightly, about 20 cents. The morning sessions had a slight impact on near-term prices, with a small increase of 34 cents, while long-term prices remained flat. In the afternoon sessions, near-term prices were relatively stable due to purchases by outsiders, while long-term buying interest was weak. Although there were few large-scale sell-offs in the market due to the loosening of spot foreign wheat, sentiment remained uneasy. Therefore, the overall outcome was weak and lackluster. If foreign wheat continues to be contracted or included in the standard, changes in the future are inevitable. As a result, the prices for November and December remained unchanged, January increased by 0.2 cents, and February increased by 0.4 cents. The spot wheat market was generally stable, with Wuhe wheat opening at 3.86 yuan, and Suzhou, Shandong, Bengbu, and Jiangbei wheat opening at 3.84 yuan, totaling 40,000 bags, reportedly handled by Fuxin and Fufeng.

After the Canadian Government Restricted Grain Speculation

Chicago Wheat Prices Plunge by More Than Two Cents 227

After several meetings between the head of wheat, McFarland, and the Canadian Prime Minister, it was announced today (29th) in Chicago that the Canadian government had decided to restrict speculation in grain trading in Winnipeg. However, the nature of the restrictions has not yet been clarified, causing panic selling in the market. Market sentiment in various places was affected. The Chicago market was in a state of confusion. Various pieces of positive news, such as reduced warehouse inventories and a deteriorating situation in Argentina with concerns about crop rot, were ignored. Prices plummeted by more than two cents. The domestic situation remains favorable for the bulls. It is generally believed that the possibility of rising prices here depends entirely on the progress of the overseas market.
